</div></th><td>17 November 1879</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td>right</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Calling code</th><td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%2B243" title="+243">+243</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:CD" title="ISO 3166-2:CD">CD</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.cd" title=".cd">.cd</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Democratic Republic of the Congo</b> (<span style="font-size:85%;"><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ec/En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg" title="En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg">pronunciation</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>&#183;<a href="/wiki/File:En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg" title="File:En-DRC-pronunciation.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></span> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">R&#233;publique d&#233;mocratique du Congo</i> <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[k&#596;&#771;&#609;o]</a></span>), also known as <b>DR Congo</b>, the <b>DRC</b>, <b>DROC</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starbird_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starbird-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USTR_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-USTR-8">[8]</a></sup> <b>Congo-Kinshasa</b>, or simply <b>the Congo</b>, is a country located in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It is sometimes anachronistically referred to by its former name of <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>, which was its official name between 1971 and 1997. It is, by area, the largest country in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, the second-largest in all of Africa (after <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">11th-largest in the world</a>. With a population of over 78 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup> the Democratic Republic of the Congo is the most populated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_French_is_an_official_language" title="List of countries where French is an official language">officially Francophone country</a>, the fourth-most-populated country in Africa, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" title="List of countries by population">16th-most-populated country in the world</a>.\n</p><p>Centred on the Congo Basin, the territory of the DRC was first inhabited by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_African_foragers" title="Central African foragers">Central African foragers</a> around 90,000 years ago and was reached by the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> about 3,000 years ago. In the west, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a> ruled around the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> from the 14th to 19th centuries. In the centre and east, the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Luba" title="Kingdom of Luba">Luba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lunda" title="Kingdom of Lunda">Lunda</a> ruled from the 16th and 17th centuries to the 19th century. In the 1870s, just before the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>, European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Congo_Basin" title="Exploration of the Congo Basin">exploration of the Congo Basin</a> was carried out, first led by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morton_Stanley" title="Henry Morton Stanley">Henry Morton Stanley</a> under the sponsorship of King <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">Leopold II of Belgium</a>. Leopold formally acquired rights to the Congo territory at the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> in 1885 and made the land his private property, naming it the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>. During the Free State, the <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial</a> military unit, the <i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a>,</i> forced the local population to produce <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">rubber</a>, and from 1885 to 1908, millions of Congolese died as a consequence of <a href="/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State" title="Atrocities in the Congo Free State">disease and exploitation</a>. In 1908, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, despite initial reluctance, formally <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium#Relinquishment_of_the_Congo" title="Leopold II of Belgium">annexed</a> the Free State, which became the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>.\n</p><p>The Belgian Congo achieved independence on 30 June 1960 under the name <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)">Republic of the Congo</a>. <a href="/wiki/Congolese_nationalism_(Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo)" title="Congolese nationalism (Democratic Republic of the Congo)">Congolese nationalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a> was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo_general_election,_1960" title="Belgian Congo general election, 1960">elected</a> the first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Joseph Kasa-Vubu</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">President</a>. Conflict arose over the administration of the territory, which became known as the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">Katanga</a>, under <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%AFse_Tshombe" title="Mo&#239;se Tshombe">Mo&#239;se Tshombe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Kasai" title="South Kasai">South Kasai</a> attempted to secede. After Lumumba turned to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> for assistance in the crisis, the U.S. and Belgium became wary and oversaw his removal from office by Kasa-Vubu on 5 September and ultimate execution by Belgian-led Katangese troops on 17 January 1961. On 25 November 1965, Army Chief of Staff Joseph-D&#233;sir&#233; Mobutu, who later renamed himself <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a>, officially came into power through <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis#Second_Mobutu_coup_d\'&#233;tat" title="Congo Crisis">a coup d\'&#233;tat</a>. In 1971, he renamed the country <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>. The country was run as a <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorial</a> <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a>, with his <a href="/wiki/Popular_Movement_of_the_Revolution" title="Popular Movement of the Revolution">Popular Movement of the Revolution</a> as the sole legal party. Mobutu\'s government received considerable support from the United States, due to its anti-communist stance during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. By the early 1990s, Mobutu\'s government began to weaken. Destabilisation in the east resulting from the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a> and disenfranchisement among the eastern <a href="/wiki/Banyamulenge" title="Banyamulenge">Banyamulenge</a> (Congolese Tutsi) population led to a 1996 invasion led by <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a> <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Patriotic_Front" title="Rwandan Patriotic Front">FPR</a>-ruled Rwanda, which began the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 May 1997, <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-D&#233;sir&#233; Kabila">Laurent-D&#233;sir&#233; Kabila</a>, a leader of Tutsi forces from the province of <a href="/wiki/South_Kivu" title="South Kivu">South Kivu</a>, became President after Mobutu fled to <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, reverting the country\'s name to the Democratic Republic of the Congo. Tensions between President Kabila and the Rwandan and Tutsi presence in the country led to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a> from 1998 to 2003. Ultimately, nine African countries and around twenty armed groups became involved in the war,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowers2_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bowers2-9">[9]</a></sup> which resulted in the deaths of 5.4 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRC2007fullreport_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRC2007fullreport-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_deadliest_war_in_the_world_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_deadliest_war_in_the_world-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRC2007Facts_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRC2007Facts-13">[13]</a></sup> The two wars devastated the country. President Laurent-D&#233;sir&#233; Kabila was assassinated by one of his bodyguards on 16 January 2001 and was succeeded eight days later as President by his son <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph</a>.\n</p><p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo is extremely rich in <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> but has had <a href="/wiki/Fragile_state" title="Fragile state">political instability</a>, a lack of infrastructure, issues with corruption and centuries of both commercial and colonial extraction and exploitation with little holistic development. Besides the capital <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>, the two next largest cities <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mbuji-Mayi" title="Mbuji-Mayi">Mbuji-Mayi</a> are both mining communities. DR Congo\'s largest export is raw minerals, with China accepting over 50% of DRC\'s exports in 2012. In 2016, DR Congo\'s level of human development was ranked 176th out of 187 countries by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDI_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-HDI-6">[6]</a></sup> As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, around 600,000 Congolese have fled to neighbouring countries from conflicts in the centre and east of the DRC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Two million children risk starvation, and the fighting has displaced 4.5 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">COMESA</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Sports"><span also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-54"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Citations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-55"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-56"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-57"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a></div>\n<p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo is named after the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>, which flows throughout the country. The Congo River is the world\'s deepest river and the world\'s second largest river <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_discharge" title="List of rivers by discharge">by discharge</a>. The <i>Comit&#233; d\'&#233;tudes du haut Congo</i> ("Committee for the Study of the Upper Congo"), established by <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold II of Belgium</a> in 1876, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_the_Congo" title="International Association of the Congo">International Association of the Congo</a>, established by him in 1879, were also named after the river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Congo River itself was named by early European sailors after the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> inhabitants, the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a>, when they encountered them in the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The word <i>Kongo</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kongo language</a> (also called <i>Kikongo</i>). According to American writer Samuel Henry Nelson "It is probable that the word \'Kongo\' itself implies a public gathering and that it is based on the root <i>konga</i>, \'to gather\' (trans[itive])."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The modern name of the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a>, <i>Bakongo</i> was introduced in the early 20th century.\n</p><p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo has been known in the past as, in chronological order, the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)">Republic of Congo-L&#233;opoldville</a>, the Democratic Republic of the Congo and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Zaire" title="Republic of Zaire">Republic of Zaire</a>, before returning to its current name the Democratic Republic of the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the time of independence, the country was named the Republic of Congo-L&#233;opoldville to distinguish it from its neighbour the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo-Brazzaville</a>. With the promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Luluabourg_Constitution" title="Luluabourg Constitution">Luluabourg Constitution</a> on 1 August 1964, the country became the DRC, but was renamed to <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> (a past name for the Congo River) on 27 October 1971 by President <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> as part of his <i><a href="/wiki/Authenticit%C3%A9_(Zaire)" title="Authenticit&#233; (Zaire)">Authenticit&#233;</a></i> initiative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The word <i>Zaire</i> is from a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> adaptation of a <a href="/wiki/Kongo_language" title="Kongo language">Kikongo</a> word <i>nzere</i> ("river"), a truncation of <i>nzadi o nzere</i> ("river swallowing rivers").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The river was known as <i>Zaire</i> during the 16th and 17th centuries; <i>Congo</i> seems to have replaced <i>Zaire</i> gradually in English usage during the 18th century, and <i>Congo</i> is the preferred English name in 19th-century literature, although references to <i>Zaire</i> as the name used by the natives (i.e. derived from Portuguese usage) remained common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1992, the Sovereign National Conference voted to change the name of the country to the "Democratic Republic of the Congo", but the change was not made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The country\'s name was restored by President <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-D&#233;sir&#233; Kabila">Laurent-D&#233;sir&#233; Kabila</a> following the fall of Mobutu in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. href="/wiki/History_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="History of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">History of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Congolese_history" title="Early Congolese history">Early Congolese history</a></div>\n<p>The area now known as the DRC was populated as early as 90,000 years ago, as shown by the 1988 discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Semliki_harpoon" title="Semliki harpoon">Semliki harpoon</a> at <a href="/wiki/Katanda_Territory" title="Katanda Territory">Katanda</a>, one of the oldest barbed harpoons ever found, believed to have been used to catch <a href="/wiki/Bagrus" title="Bagrus">giant river catfish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> reached Central Africa at some point during the first millennium BC, then gradually started to expand southward. Their propagation was accelerated by the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralism</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> techniques.\nThe people living in the south and southwest were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_African_foragers" title="Central African foragers">foraging</a> groups, whose technology involved only minimal use of metal technologies. The development of metal tools during this time period revolutionized agriculture and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>. This led to the displacement of the hunter-gatherer groups in the east and southeast.\nThe final wave of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> was complete by the 10th century, followed by the establishment of the Bantu kingdoms, whose rising populations soon made possible intricate local, regional and foreign commercial networks that traded mostly in slaves, salt, iron and copper.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Congo_Free_State_.281877.E2.80.931908.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Congo_Free_State_(1877&#8211;1908)">Congo Free State (1877&#8211;1908)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Congo Free State (1877&#8211;1908)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_the_Congo" title="Colonisation of the Congo">Colonisation of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State" title="Atrocities in the Congo Free State">Atrocities in the Congo Free State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Arab_war" title="Congo Arab war">Congo Arab war</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dhanis_Expedition.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2844" data-file-width="2136" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dhanis_Expedition.JPG/170px-Dhanis_Expedition.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dhanis_Expedition.JPG/255px-Dhanis_Expedition.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dhanis_Expedition.JPG/340px-Dhanis_Expedition.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dhanis_Expedition.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A contemporary depiction of a Belgian expedition during the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Arab_war" title="Congo Arab war">Congo Arab war</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="947" data-file-width="1343" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/220px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg/440px-Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stanley_Founding_of_Congo_Free_State_186_View_of_Leopoldville_Station_and_Port_1884_The_Baptist_Mission_on_the_summit_of_Leopold_Hill.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Leopoldville</a> Station and Port in 1884</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian exploration</a> and administration took place from the 1870s until the 1920s. It was first led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Henry_Morton_Stanley" title="Sir Henry Morton Stanley">Sir Henry Morton Stanley</a>, who undertook his explorations under the sponsorship of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="King Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold II of Belgium</a>. The eastern regions of the precolonial Congo were heavily disrupted by constant <a href="/wiki/Slave_raiding" title="Slave raiding">slave raiding</a>, mainly from Arab&#8211;Swahili <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">slave traders</a> such as the infamous <a href="/wiki/Tippu_Tip" title="Tippu Tip">Tippu Tip</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> who was well known to Stanley.\n</p><p>Leopold had designs on what was to become the Congo as a colony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfskeyes_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-cfskeyes-28">[28]</a></sup> In a succession of negotiations, Leopold, professing humanitarian objectives in his capacity as chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Front_organization" title="Front organization">front organization</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_Internationale_Africaine" title="Association Internationale Africaine">Association Internationale Africaine</a></i>, actually played one European rival against another.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Leopold formally acquired rights to the Congo territory at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conference_of_Berlin" title="Conference of Berlin">Conference of Berlin</a> in 1885 and made the land his private property. He named it the Congo Free State.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfskeyes_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-cfskeyes-28">[28]</a></sup> Leopold\'s regime began various infrastructure projects, such as construction of the <a href="/wiki/Matadi%E2%80%93Kinshasa_Railway" title="Matadi&#8211;Kinshasa Railway">railway that ran from the coast to the capital</a> of Leopoldville (now Kinshasa), which took eight years to complete. Nearly all such infrastructure projects were aimed at making it easier to increase the assets which Leopold and his associates could extract from the colony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b1_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-b1-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the Free State, colonists coerced the local population into producing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rubber" title="Rubber">rubber</a>, for which the spread of automobiles and development of rubber tires created a growing international market. Rubber sales made a fortune for Leopold, who built several buildings in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a> to honor himself and his country. To enforce the rubber quotas, the army, the <i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i>, was called in and made the practice of cutting off the limbs of the natives a matter of policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google748_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-google748-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the period of 1885&#8211;1908, millions of Congolese died as a consequence of exploitation and disease. In some areas the population declined dramatically&#160;&#8211; it has been estimated that <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> killed nearly half the population in the areas surrounding the lower <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google748_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-google748-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>News of the abuses began to circulate. In 1904, the British consul at Boma in the Congo, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Casement" title="Roger Casement">Roger Casement</a> was instructed by the British government to investigate. His report, called the <a href="/wiki/Casement_Report" title="Casement Report">Casement Report</a>, confirmed the accusations of humanitarian abuses. The Belgian Parliament forced Leopold II to set up an independent commission of inquiry. Its findings confirmed Casement\'s report of absuses, concluding that the population of the Congo had been "reduced by half" during this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b1_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-b1-29">[29]</a></sup> Determining precisely how many people died is impossible, as no accurate records exist.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Belgian_Congo_.281908.E2.80.9360.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgian_Congo_(1908&#8211;60)">Belgian Congo (1908&#8211;60)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Belgian Congo (1908&#8211;60)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a></div>\n<p>In 1908, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_parliament" title="Belgian parliament">Belgian parliament</a>, in spite of initial reluctance, bowed to international pressure (especially from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>) and took over the Free State from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Leopold_II" title="King Leopold II">King Leopold II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 October 1908, the Belgian parliament voted in favour of annexing the Congo as a Belgian <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a>. Executive power went to the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Colonies_(Belgium)" title="Minister of the Colonies (Belgium)">Belgian minister of colonial affairs</a>, assisted by a Colonial Council (Conseil Colonial) (both located in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>). The Belgian parliament exercised legislative authority over the Belgian Congo. In 1926 the colonial capital moved from Boma to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opoldville" title="L&#233;opoldville">L&#233;opoldville</a>, some 300 kilometres (190&#160;mi) further upstream into the interior.\n</p><p>The transition from the Congo Free State to the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a> was a break but it also featured a large degree of continuity. The last Governor-general of the Congo Free State, Baron <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9ophile_Wahis" title="Th&#233;ophile Wahis">Th&#233;ophile Wahis</a>, remained in office in the Belgian Congo and the majority of Leopold II\'s administration with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Opening up the Congo and its natural and mineral riches to the Belgian economy remained the main motive for colonial expansion&#160;&#8211; however, other priorities, such as healthcare and basic education, slowly gained in importance.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="974" data-file-width="972" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/220px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/330px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg/440px-Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Congo_belge_campagne_1918.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i> soldiers in the Belgian Congo in 1918. At its peak, the Force Publique had around 19,000 African soldiers, led by 420 white officers.</div></div></div>\n<p>Colonial administrators ruled the territory and a dual legal system existed (a system of European courts and another one of indigenous courts, <i>tribunaux indig&#232;nes</i>). Indigenous courts had only limited powers and remained under the firm control of the colonial administration. Records show that in 1936, 728 Belgian administrators ran the colony.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Belgian authorities permitted no political activity in the Congo whatsoever,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a></i>, a locally-recruited army under Belgian command, put down any attempts at rebellion.\n</p><p>The Belgian population of the colony increased from 1,928 in 1910 to nearly 89,000 in 1959.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The Belgian Congo was directly involved in the two world wars. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> (1914&#8211;1918), an initial stand-off between the <i>Force Publique</i> and the German colonial army in <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tanganyika" title="Tanganyika">Tanganyika</a>) turned into open warfare with a joint Anglo-Belgian invasion of German colonial territory in 1916 and 1917 during the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_I)" title="East African Campaign (World War I)">East African Campaign</a>. The <i>Force Publique</i> gained a notable victory when it marched into <a href="/wiki/Tabora" title="Tabora">Tabora</a> in September 1916 under the command of General <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tombeur" title="Charles Tombeur">Charles Tombeur</a> after heavy fighting.\n</p><p>After 1918, Belgium was rewarded for the participation of the <i>Force Publique</i> in the East African campaign with a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> mandate over the previously German colony of <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Belgian Congo provided a crucial source of income for the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_government_in_exile" title="Belgian government in exile">Belgian government-in-exile</a> in London, and the <i>Force Publique</i> again participated in Allied campaigns in Africa. Belgian Congolese forces under the command of Belgian officers notably fought against the Italian colonial army in Ethiopia in <a href="/wiki/Asosa" title="Asosa">Asosa</a>, Borta&#239;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sa%C3%AFo" title="Siege of Sa&#239;o">Sa&#239;o</a> under Major-General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Auguste-Eduard_Gilliaert" title="Auguste-Eduard Gilliaert">Auguste-Eduard Gilliaert</a> during the second <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="East African Campaign (World War II)">East African Campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Independence_and_political_crisis_.281960.E2.80.9365.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_political_crisis_(1960&#8211;65)">Independence and political crisis (1960&#8211;65)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence and political crisis (1960&#8211;65)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)">Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="293" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png/170px-Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png/255px-Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kasa-Vubu_in_Israel.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The leader of ABAKO, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Joseph Kasa-Vubu</a>, first democratically elected President of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)">Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="467" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/220px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/330px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/440px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, first democratically elected Prime Minister of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)">Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)</a>, was murdered by Belgian-supported <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">Katangan separatists</a> in 1961</div></div></div>\n<p>In May 1960, a growing nationalist movement, the <a href="/wiki/Mouvement_National_Congolais" title="Mouvement National Congolais">Mouvement National Congolais</a> (MNC) led by <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, won the parliamentary elections. Patrice Lumumba thus became the first Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. The parliament elected as President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasavubu" title="Joseph Kasavubu">Joseph Kasavubu</a>, of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alliance_des_Bakongo" title="Alliance des Bakongo">Alliance des Bakongo</a> (ABAKO) party. Other parties that emerged included the <a href="/wiki/Parti_Solidaire_Africain" title="Parti Solidaire Africain">Parti Solidaire Africain</a> (PSA) led by <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Gizenga" title="Antoine Gizenga">Antoine Gizenga</a>, and the Parti National du Peuple (PNP) led by Albert Delvaux and <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Mbariko" title="Laurent Mbariko">Laurent Mbariko</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Belgian Congo achieved independence on 30 June 1960 under the name "R&#233;publique du Congo" ("Republic of Congo" or "Republic of the Congo" in English). As the neighboring French colony of Middle Congo (Moyen Congo) also chose the name "Republic of Congo" upon achieving its independence, the two countries were more commonly known as "Congo-L&#233;opoldville" and "Congo-Brazzaville", after their capital cities.\n</p><p>Shortly after independence the Force Publique mutinied, and on 11 July the <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">province of Katanga</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%AFse_Tshombe" title="Mo&#239;se Tshombe">Mo&#239;se Tshombe</a>) and <a href="/wiki/South_Kasai" title="South Kasai">South Kasai</a> engaged in secessionist struggles against the new leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Most of the 100,000 Europeans who had remained behind after independence fled the country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> opening the way for Congolese to replace the European military and administrative elite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>\nOn 5 September 1960, Kasavubu dismissed Lumumba from office. Lumumba declared Kasavubu\'s action unconstitutional and a crisis between the two leaders developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Events set in motion by the U.S. and Belgium on 14 September removed Lumumba from office with forces loyal to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_Mobutu" title="Joseph Mobutu">Joseph Mobutu</a>. On 17 January 1961, he was handed over to Katangan authorities and executed by Belgian-led Katangese troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> An investigation by the Belgium\'s Parliament in 2001 found Belgium "morally responsible" for the murder of Lumumba, and the country has since officially apologised for its role in his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Amidst widespread confusion and chaos, a temporary government was led by technicians the (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Coll%C3%A8ge_des_commissaires_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9raux&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Coll&#232;ge des commissaires g&#233;n&#233;raux (page does not exist)">Coll&#232;ge des commissaires g&#233;n&#233;raux</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coll%C3%A8ge_des_commissaires_g%C3%A9n%C3%A9raux" title="fr:Coll&#232;ge des commissaires g&#233;n&#233;raux">fr</a>]</span>). The secession ended in January 1963 with the assistance of UN forces. Several short-lived governments, of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_Ileo" title="Joseph Ileo">Joseph Ileo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyrille_Adoula" title="Cyrille Adoula">Cyrille Adoula</a> and Moise Tshombe, took over in quick succession.\n</p><p>Lumumba had previously appointed Joseph Mobutu chief of staff of the new Congo army, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Military of the Democratic Republic of Congo">Arm&#233;e Nationale Congolaise</a> (ANC).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Taking advantage of the leadership crisis between Kasavubu and Tshombe, Mobutu garnered enough support within the army to launch a coup. With financial support from the United States and Belgium, Mobutu paid his soldiers privately.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The aversion of Western powers to communism and leftist ideology influenced their decision to finance Mobutu\'s quest to neutralize Kasavubu and Lumumba in a coup by proxy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)_constitutional_referendum,_1964" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville) constitutional referendum, 1964">constitutional referendum</a> after Mobutu\'s coup of 1965 resulted in the country\'s official name being changed to the "Democratic Republic of the Congo."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup> In 1971 Mobutu changed the name again, this time to "Republic of Zaire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Mobutu_and_Zaire_.281965.E2.80.9397.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobutu_and_Zaire_(1965&#8211;97)">Mobutu and Zaire (1965&#8211;97)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mobutu and Zaire (1965&#8211;97)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mobutu_Nixon.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/220px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/330px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mobutu_Nixon.gif/440px-Mobutu_Nixon.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mobutu_Nixon.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> and Richard Nixon in Washington, D.C., 1973.</div></div></div>\n<p>The new president had the staunch support of the United States because of his <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">opposition</a> to Communism; the US believed that his administration would serve as an effective counter to communist movements in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> A single-party system was established, and Mobutu declared himself head of state. He periodically held elections in which he was the only candidate. Although relative peace and stability were achieved, Mobutu\'s government was guilty of severe human rights violations, political repression, a <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a> and corruption.\n</p><p>By late 1967 Mobutu had successfully neutralized his political opponents and rivals, either through co-opting them into his regime, arresting them, or rendering them otherwise politically impotent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201358_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201358-46">[46]</a></sup> Throughout the late 1960s Mobutu continued to shuffle his governments and cycle officials in and out of office to maintain control. Kasa-Vubu\'s death in April 1969 ensured that no person with First Republic credentials could challenge his rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201361&#8211;62_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201361&#8211;62-47">[47]</a></sup> By the early 1970s Mobutu was attempting to assert Zaire as a leading African nation. He traveled frequently across the continent while the government became more vocal about African issues, particularly those relating to the southern region. Zaire established semi-clientelist relationships with several smaller African states, especially Burundi, Chad, and Togo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201364_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201364-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Corruption became so common the term "<i>le mal Zairois</i>" or "Zairean Sickness",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> meaning gross corruption, theft and mismanagement, was coined, reportedly by Mobutu himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201374_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoungTurner201374-50">[50]</a></sup> International aid, most often in the form of loans, enriched Mobutu while he allowed national infrastructure such as roads to deteriorate to as little as one-quarter of what had existed in 1960. Zaire became a <a href="/wiki/Kleptocracy" title="Kleptocracy">kleptocracy</a> as Mobutu and his associates <a href="/wiki/Embezzlement" title="Embezzlement">embezzled</a> government funds.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="1740" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/220px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/330px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg/440px-Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prince_Bernhard_and_Mobutu_Sese_Seko_1973.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mobutu with the Dutch <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernhard_of_Lippe-Biesterfeld" title="Bernhard of Lippe-Biesterfeld">Prince Bernhard</a> in Kinshasa in 1973</div></div></div>\n<p>In a campaign to identify himself with African nationalism, starting on 1 June 1966, Mobutu renamed the nation\'s cities: L&#233;opoldville became <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a> [the country was now Democratic Republic of The Congo&#160;&#8211;&#160;Kinshasa], Stanleyville became <a href="/wiki/Kisangani" title="Kisangani">Kisangani</a>, Elisabethville became <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>, and Coquilhatville became <a href="/wiki/Mbandaka" title="Mbandaka">Mbandaka</a>. This renaming campaign was completed in the 1970s.\n</p><p>In 1971, Mobutu renamed the country the <i>Republic of Zaire</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kisanganibobb_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-kisanganibobb-20">[20]</a></sup> its fourth name change in 11 years and its sixth overall. The Congo River was renamed the Zaire River.\n</p><p>During the 1970s and 1980s, he was invited to visit the United States on several occasions, meeting with U.S. Presidents <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> U.S. relations with Mobutu cooled, as he was no longer deemed necessary as a <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> ally. Opponents within Zaire stepped up demands for reform. This atmosphere contributed to Mobutu\'s declaring the Third Republic in 1990, whose constitution was supposed to pave the way for democratic reform. The reforms turned out to be largely cosmetic. Mobutu continued in power until armed forces forced him to flee in 1997. "From 1990 to 1993, the United States facilitated Mobutu&#8217;s attempts to hijack political change", one academic wrote, and "also assisted the rebellion of Laurent-Desire Kabila that overthrew the Mobutu regime."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Continental_and_Civil_wars_.281996.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Continental_and_Civil_wars_(1996&#8211;present)">Continental and Civil wars (1996&#8211;present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Continental and Civil wars (1996&#8211;present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1444" data-file-width="1526" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/220px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/330px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png/440px-Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Second_Congo_War_Africa_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Belligerents of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a></div></div></div>\n<p>By 1996, following the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Civil_War" title="Rwandan Civil War">Rwandan Civil War</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rwandan_Genocide" title="Rwandan Genocide">genocide</a> and the ascension of a <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a>-led government in Rwanda, Rwandan <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> militia forces (<a href="/wiki/Interahamwe" title="Interahamwe">Interahamwe</a>) fled to eastern Zaire and used refugee camps as a base for incursions against Rwanda. They allied with the Zairian armed forces (FAZ) to launch a campaign against Congolese ethnic Tutsis in eastern Zaire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A coalition of Rwandan and Ugandan armies invaded Zaire to overthrow the government of Mobutu, and ultimately to control the mineral resources of Zaire<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, launching the <b><a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a></b>. The coalition allied with some opposition figures, led by <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-D&#233;sir&#233; Kabila">Laurent-D&#233;sir&#233; Kabila</a>, becoming the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Democratic_Forces_for_the_Liberation_of_Congo" title="Alliance of Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Congo">Alliance of Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Congo</a> (AFDL). In 1997 Mobutu fled and Kabila marched into Kinshasa, named himself president, and reverted the name of the country to the Democratic Republic of the Congo.\n</p><p>Kabila later requested that foreign military forces return to their own countries. He had concerns that the Rwandan officers running his army were plotting to give the presidency to a Tutsi who would report directly to Rwandan president, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kagame" title="Paul Kagame">Paul Kagame</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Rwandan troops retreated to Goma and launched a new Tutsi-led rebel military movement called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rassemblement_Congolais_pour_la_Democratie" title="Rassemblement Congolais pour la Democratie">Rassemblement Congolais pour la Democratie</a> (RCD) to fight Kabila, while Uganda instigated the creation of new rebel movement called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Congo" title="Movement for the Liberation of Congo">Movement for the Liberation of Congo</a> (MLC), led by Congolese warlord <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Bemba" title="Jean-Pierre Bemba">Jean-Pierre Bemba</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The two rebel movements, along with Rwandan and Ugandan troops, started the <b><a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a></b> by attacking the DRC army in 1998. Angolan, Zimbabwean and Namibian militaries entered the hostilities on the side of the government.\n</p><p>Kabila was assassinated in 2001. His son <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> succeeded him and called for multilateral peace-talks. UN peacekeepers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MONUC" title="MONUC">MONUC</a>, now known as MONUSCO, arrived in April 2001. In 2002 and 2003 Bemba intervened in the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> on behalf of its former president, <a href="/wiki/Ange-F%C3%A9lix_Patass%C3%A9" title="Ange-F&#233;lix Patass&#233;">Ange-F&#233;lix Patass&#233;</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Talks led to a peace accord under which Kabila would share power with former rebels. By June 2003 all foreign armies except those of Rwanda had pulled out of Congo. A <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Government_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Transitional Government of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">transitional government</a> was set up until after the election. A constitution was approved by voters, and on 30 July 2006 DRC held its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election,_2006" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo general election, 2006">first multi-party elections</a>. An election-result dispute between Kabila and Jean-Pierre Bemba turned into an all-out battle between their supporters in the streets of <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>. MONUC took control of the city. A new election took place in October 2006, which Kabila won, and on December 2006 he was sworn in as President.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/220px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/330px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg/440px-Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Refugees_in_Congo.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Refugees in the Congo</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kivu_conflict">Kivu conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kivu conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kivu_Conflict" title="Kivu Conflict">Kivu Conflict</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Laurent_Nkunda" title="Laurent Nkunda">Laurent Nkunda</a>, a member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RCD-Goma" title="RCD-Goma">RCD-Goma</a>, an RCD branch integrated to the army, defected along with troops loyal to him and formed the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_for_the_Defence_of_the_People" title="National Congress for the Defence of the People">National Congress for the Defence of the People</a> (CNDP), which began an armed rebellion against the government, starting the <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">Kivu conflict</a>. They were believed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2015)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to be again backed by Rwanda as a way to tackle the <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> group, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Forces_for_the_Liberation_of_Rwanda" title="Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Rwanda">Democratic Forces for the Liberation of Rwanda</a> (FDLR). In March 2009, after a deal between the DRC and Rwanda, Rwandan troops entered the DRC and arrested Nkunda and were allowed to pursue FDLR militants. The CNDP signed a peace treaty with the government in which it agreed to become a political party and to have its soldiers intigrated into the national army in exchange for the release of its imprisoned members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In 2012 <a href="/wiki/Bosco_Ntaganda" title="Bosco Ntaganda">Bosco Ntaganda</a>, the leader of the CNDP, and troops loyal to him, mutinied and formed the rebel military <a href="/wiki/March_23_Movement" title="March 23 Movement">March 23 Movement</a>, claiming the government violated the treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the resulting <a href="/wiki/M23_rebellion" title="M23 rebellion">M23 rebellion</a>, M23 briefly captured the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a> in November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Neighboring countries, particularly Rwanda, have been accused of arming rebels groups and using them as proxies to gain control of the resource-rich country, an accusation they deny.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In March 2013, the United Nations <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Security_Council" title="Security Council">Security Council</a> authorized the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">United Nations Force Intervention Brigade</a>, the first offensive <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> peacekeeping unit, to neutralize armed groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN1_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN1-61">[61]</a></sup> On 5 November 2013, M23 declared an end to its insurgency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(6988913212).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/220px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/330px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg/440px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%286988913212%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(6988913212).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People fleeing their villages due to fighting between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Military of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">FARDC</a> and rebel groups, <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a>, 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>Additionally, in northern <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mai-Mai" title="Mai-Mai">Mai-Mai</a> created by Laurent Kabila slipped out of the control of Kinshasa with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G%C3%A9d%C3%A9on_Kyungu_Mutanga" title="G&#233;d&#233;on Kyungu Mutanga">G&#233;d&#233;on Kyungu Mutanga</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mai_Mai_Kata_Katanga" title="Mai Mai Kata Katanga">Mai Mai Kata Katanga</a> briefly invading the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> in 2013 and 400,000 persons displaced in the province as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On and off fighting in the <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a> occurred between the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_and_Integrationist_Front" title="Nationalist and Integrationist Front">Nationalist and Integrationist Front</a> (FNI) and the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Congolese_Patriots" title="Union of Congolese Patriots">Union of Congolese Patriots</a> (UPC) who claimed to represent the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lendu" title="Lendu">Lendu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hema_people" title="Hema people">Hema</a> ethnic groups, respectively. In the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kony" title="Joseph Kony">Joseph Kony</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LRA" title="LRA">LRA</a> moved from their original bases in Uganda and South Sudan to DR Congo in 2005 and set up camps in the Garamba National Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009, <i>The New York Times</i> reported that people in the Congo continued to die at a rate of an estimated 45,000 per month<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>&#160;&#8211; estimates of the number who have died from the long conflict range from 900,000 to 5,400,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The death toll is due to widespread disease and famine; reports indicate that almost half of the individuals who have died are children under five years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> There have been frequent reports of weapon bearers killing civilians, of the destruction of property, of widespread sexual violence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> causing hundreds of thousands of people to flee their homes, and of other breaches of humanitarian and human rights law. One study found that more than <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">400,000 women are raped</a> in the Democratic Republic of Congo every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The war in the Congo has been described as the bloodiest war since World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On 8 December 2017, fourteen UN soldiers and five Congolese regular soldiers were killed in a rebel attack at Semuliki in Beni territory. The rebels were thought to be <a href="/wiki/Allied_Democratic_Forces" title="Allied Democratic Forces">Allied Democratic Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> UN investigations confirmed that aggressor in the December attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_(21_May_2013)_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._(8782972992).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146"
