srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/330px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg/440px-FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_%2821_May_2013%29_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._%288782972992%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FARDC_and_MONUSCO_reinforce_their_presence_in_and_around_Goma_following_a_second_day_(21_May_2013)_of_clashes_between_M23_and_National_troops._(8782972992).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Government troops near <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a> during the <a href="/wiki/M23_rebellion" title="M23 rebellion">M23 rebellion</a> in May 2013</div></div></div>\n<h3><span id="Kabila.27s_term_in_office_and_multiple_anti-government_protests"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kabila\'s_term_in_office_and_multiple_anti-government_protests">Kabila\'s term in office and multiple anti-government protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kabila\'s term in office and multiple anti-government protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2015, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015_Congolese_protests" title="2015 Congolese protests">major protests</a> broke out across the country and protesters demanded that <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> step down as President. The protests began after the passage of a law by the Congolese lower house that, if also passed by the Congolese upper house, would keep Kabila in power at least until a national census was conducted (a process which would likely take several years and therefore keep him in power past the planned 2016 elections, which he is constitutionally barred from participating in).\n</p><p>This bill passed; however, it was gutted of the provision that would keep Joseph Kabila in power until a census took place. A census is supposed to take place, but it is no longer tied to when the elections take place. In 2015, elections were scheduled for late 2016 and a tenuous peace held in the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_DRC_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_DRC-74">[74]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 November Congolese foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Tshibanda" title="Raymond Tshibanda">Raymond Tshibanda</a> told the press no elections would be held in 2016, after 20 December, the end of president Kabila\'s term. In a conference in Madagascar, Tshibanda said that Kabila\'s government had "consulted election experts" from Congo, the United Nations and elsewhere, and that "it has been decided that the voter registration operation will end on July 31, 2017, and that elections will take place in April 2018."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/December_2016_Congolese_protests" title="December 2016 Congolese protests">Protests broke out in the country on 20 December</a> when Kabila\'s term in office ended. Across the country dozens of protesters were killed and hundreds were arrested.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Upsurge_in_violence">Upsurge in violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Upsurge in violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ituri_conflict" title="Ituri conflict">Ituri conflict</a></div>\n<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Jan_Egeland" title="Jan Egeland">Jan Egeland</a>, presently Secretary General of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Refugee_Council" title="Norwegian Refugee Council">Norwegian Refugee Council</a>, the situation in the DRC became much worse in 2016 and 2017 and is a major moral and humanitarian challenge comparable to the wars in Syria and Yemen, which receive much more attention. Women and children are abused sexually and "abused in all possible manners". Besides the conflict in <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a>, violence has gone up in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kasai_region" title="Kasai region">Kasai region</a>. The armed groups are after <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a> to line the pockets of rich men both in the region and internationally. There are also ethnic and cultural rivalries at play, as well as religious motives and the political crisis with postponed elections. He says people believe the situation in the DRC is "stably bad" but in fact it has become much, much worse. "The big wars of the Congo that were really on top of the agenda 15 years ago are back and worsening".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Due to disruption of planting and harvesting caused by the conflict, the UN estimated in March 2018 that two million children risk starvation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Human Rights Watch said in 2017 that Joseph Kabila recruited former M23 fighters to put down country-wide protests over his refusal to step down from office at the end of his term. "M23 fighters patrolled the streets of Congo&#8217;s main cities, firing on or arresting protesters or anyone else deemed to be a threat to the president," they said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fierce fighting has erupted in Masisi between government forces and a powerful local warlord, General Delta. The United Nations mission in the DRC is its largest and most expensive peacekeeping effort, but it shut down five UN bases near Masisi in 2017, after the US led a push to cut costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tribal_conflict">Tribal conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tribal conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2018_Yumbi_violence" title="2018 Yumbi violence">2018 Yumbi violence</a></div>\n<p>A tribal conflict erupted on 16-17 December 2018 at <a href="/wiki/Yumbi" title="Yumbi">Yumbi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mai-Ndombe_Province" title="Mai-Ndombe Province">Mai-Ndombe Province</a>, 400 km (250 miles) north of Kinshasa. Nearly 900 Banunu people from four villages were slaughtered by members of the Batende community in a deep-rooted rivalry over monthly tribal duties, land, fields and water resources. Some 100 Banunus fled to Moniende island in the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>, and another 16,000 to <a href="/wiki/Makotimpoko_District" title="Makotimpoko District">Makotimpoko District</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Congo" title="Republic of Congo">Republic of Congo</a>. Military-style tactics were employed in the bloodbath, and some assailants were clothed in army uniforms. Local authorities and elements within the security forces were suspected of lending them support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afp1_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-afp1-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_election_and_new_president">2018 election and new president</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2018 election and new president">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On December 30, 2018 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_general_election,_2018" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo general election, 2018">presidential election to determine the successor to Kabila was held</a>. On January 10, 2019, the electoral commission announced opposition candidate <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Tshisekedi" title="F&#233;lix Tshisekedi">F&#233;lix Tshisekedi</a> as the winner of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> He was officially sworn in as President on January 24, 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inaug_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-inaug-82">[82]</a></sup> However, there were widespread suspicions that the results were rigged and that a deal had been made between Tshisekedi and Kabila. The Catholic Church said that the official results did not correspond to the information its election monitors had collected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The government had also "delayed" the vote until March in some areas, citing the <a href="/wiki/2018_Kivu_Ebola_outbreak" title="2018 Kivu Ebola outbreak">Ebola outbreak in Kivu</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Kivu_conflict" title="Kivu conflict">the ongoing military conflict</a>. This was criticized as these regions are known as opposition strongholds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. href="/wiki/File:Cg-map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="330" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cg-map.png/220px-Cg-map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Cg-map.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cg-map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The map of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Democratic Republic of the Congo map of K&#246;ppen climate classification</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Geography of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Geography of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Geology of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Geology of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC) is located in central <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>, bordered to the northwest by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>, to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, to the northeast by <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, to the east by <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, and by <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> (across <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>), to the south and southeast by <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, to the southwest by <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, and to the west by the South <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda Province exclave of Angola</a>. The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_parallel_north" title="6th parallel north">6&#176;N</a> and <a href="/wiki/14th_parallel_south" title="14th parallel south">14&#176;S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_east" title="32nd meridian east">32&#176;E</a>. It straddles the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>, with one-third to the North and two-thirds to the South. The size of Congo, 2,345,408 square kilometres (905,567&#160;sq&#160;mi), is slightly greater than the combined areas of Spain, France, Germany, Sweden, and Norway. It is the second largest country in Africa by area, after <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>.\n</p><p>As a result of its equatorial location, the DRC experiences high precipitation and has the highest frequency of thunderstorms in the world. The annual rainfall can total upwards of 2,000 millimetres (80&#160;in) in some places, and the area sustains the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_Rainforest" title="Congo Rainforest">Congo Rainforest</a>, the second-largest rain forest in the world after the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon</a>. This massive expanse of lush jungle covers most of the vast, low-lying central <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">basin</a> of the river, which slopes toward the Atlantic Ocean in the west. This area is surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaus</a> merging into <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a> in the south and southwest, by mountainous terraces in the west, and dense <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> extending beyond the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> in the north. High, glaciated mountains (<a href="/wiki/Rwenzori_Mountains" title="Rwenzori Mountains">Rwenzori Mountains</a>) are found in the extreme eastern region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rainforest_-_Ituri_(20874628148).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg/220px-Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg/330px-Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg/440px-Rainforest_-_Ituri_%2820874628148%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rainforest_-_Ituri_(20874628148).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ituri_Rainforest" title="Ituri Rainforest">Ituri Rainforest</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> also produced the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> system which dominates the region topographically along with the rainforest it flows through, though they are not mutually exclusive. The name for the Congo state is derived in part from the river. The river basin (meaning the Congo River and all of its myriad tributaries) occupies nearly the entire country and an area of nearly 1,000,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (390,000&#160;sq&#160;mi). The river and its tributaries form the backbone of Congolese economics and transportation. Major tributaries include the <a href="/wiki/Kasai_River" title="Kasai River">Kasai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sangha_River" title="Sangha River">Sangha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruzizi_River" title="Ruzizi River">Ruzizi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aruwimi" title="Aruwimi">Aruwimi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lulonga_River" title="Lulonga River">Lulonga</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dem_congo_sat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2261" data-file-width="2293" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Dem_congo_sat.jpg/220px-Dem_congo_sat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Dem_congo_sat.jpg/330px-Dem_congo_sat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Dem_congo_sat.jpg/440px-Dem_congo_sat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dem_congo_sat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite image of Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>\n<p>The sources of the Congo are in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift_Mountains" title="Albertine Rift Mountains">Albertine Rift Mountains</a> that flank the western branch of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Rift" title="East African Rift">East African Rift</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mweru" title="Lake Mweru">Lake Mweru</a>. The river flows generally west from <a href="/wiki/Kisangani" title="Kisangani">Kisangani</a> just below <a href="/wiki/Boyoma_Falls" title="Boyoma Falls">Boyoma Falls</a>, then gradually bends southwest, passing by <a href="/wiki/Mbandaka" title="Mbandaka">Mbandaka</a>, joining with the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a>, and running into the <a href="/wiki/Pool_Malebo" title="Pool Malebo">Pool Malebo</a> (Stanley Pool). <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a> are on opposite sides of the river at the Pool. Then the river narrows and falls through a number of cataracts in deep canyons, collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Livingstone_Falls" title="Livingstone Falls">Livingstone Falls</a>, and runs past <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boma,_Congo" title="Boma, Congo">Boma</a> into the Atlantic Ocean. The river also has the second-largest flow and the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watershed</a> of any river in the world (trailing the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a> in both respects). The river and a 37 kilometres (23&#160;mi) wide strip of coastline on its north bank provide the country\'s only outlet to the Atlantic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift" title="Albertine Rift">Albertine Rift</a> plays a key role in shaping the Congo\'s geography. Not only is the northeastern section of the country much more mountainous, but due to the rift\'s <a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">tectonic</a> activity, this area also experiences <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> activity, occasionally with loss of life. The geologic activity in this area also created the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a>, three of which lie on the Congo\'s eastern frontier: <a href="/wiki/Lake_Albert_(Africa)" title="Lake Albert (Africa)">Lake Albert</a> (known during the Mobutu era as Lake Mobutu Sese Seko), <a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a> (Unknown until late 1712), <a href="/wiki/Lake_Edward" title="Lake Edward">Lake Edward</a> (known during the <a href="/wiki/Idi_Amin" title="Idi Amin">Amin</a> era as Lake Idi Amin Dada), and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>. Lake Edward and Lake Albert are connected by the <a href="/wiki/Semliki_River" title="Semliki River">Semliki River</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Rift_valley" title="Rift valley">Rift valley</a> has exposed an enormous amount of mineral wealth throughout the south and east of the Congo, making it accessible to mining. <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">Cobalt</a>, copper, <a href="/wiki/Cadmium" title="Cadmium">cadmium</a>, industrial and gem-quality <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diamonds" title="Diamonds">diamonds</a>, gold, silver, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanium" title="Germanium">germanium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radium" title="Radium">radium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>, iron ore, and coal are all found in plentiful supply, especially in the Congo\'s southeastern Katanga region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1680" data-file-width="2928" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg/220px-An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg/330px-An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:An_aerial_view_of_the_towering_volcanic_peak_of_Mt._Nyiragongo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Nyiragongo" title="Mount Nyiragongo">Mount Nyiragongo</a>, which last erupted in 2002.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_rivi%C3%A8re_Lulilaka,_parc_national_de_Salonga,_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="344" href="/wiki/Salonga_National_Park" title="Salonga National Park">Salonga National Park</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paysage_du_territoire_de_Masisi_(28130228449).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="1383" decoding="async" height="165" title="Masisi Territory">Masisi Territory</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nord-Kivu,_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._(22722760943).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg/330px-Nord-Kivu%2C_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._%2822722760943%29.jpg 1.5x, 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nord-Kivu,_RD_Congo_-_Vue_sur_un_crat%C3%A8re_aux_abords_de_la_ville_de_Goma._(22722760943).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Kivu" title="North Kivu">North Kivu</a> province</div></div></div>\n<p>On 17 January 2002 <a href="/wiki/Mount_Nyiragongo" title="Mount Nyiragongo">Mount Nyiragongo</a> erupted in Congo, with the lava running out at 64&#160;km/h (40&#160;mph) and 46&#160;m (50&#160;yd) wide. One of the three streams of extremely fluid lava flowed through the nearby city of <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a>, killing 45 and leaving 120,000 homeless. Four hundred thousand people were evacuated from the city during the eruption. The lava poisoned the water of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a>, killing fish. Only two planes left the local airport because of the possibility of the explosion of stored petrol. The lava passed the airport but ruined the runway, trapping several airplanes. Six months after the 2002 eruption, nearby <a href="/wiki/Nyamuragira" title="Nyamuragira">Mount Nyamuragira</a> also erupted. Mount Nyamuragira then erupted in 2006 and again in January 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a> located in the Congo include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Central_Congolian_lowland_forests" title="Central Congolian lowland forests">Central Congolian lowland forests</a>&#160;&#8211; home to the rare <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">bonobo</a> primate</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Congolian_swamp_forests" title="Eastern Congolian swamp forests">Eastern Congolian swamp forests</a> along the Congo River</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Congolian_lowland_forests" title="Northeastern Congolian lowland forests">Northeastern Congolian lowland forests</a>, with one of the richest concentrations of primates in the world</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Congolian_forest-savanna_mosaic" title="Southern Congolian forest-savanna mosaic">Southern Congolian forest-savanna mosaic</a></li>\n<li>A large section of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Zambezian_Miombo_woodlands" title="Central Zambezian Miombo woodlands">Central Zambezian Miombo woodlands</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift_montane_forests" title="Albertine Rift montane forests">Albertine Rift montane forests</a> region of high forest runs along the eastern borders of the country.</li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> located in Democratic Republic of Congo are:\n<a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga National Park</a> (1979),\n<a href="/wiki/Garamba_National_Park" title="Garamba National Park">Garamba National Park</a> (1980),\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kahuzi-Biega_National_Park" title="Kahuzi-Biega National Park">Kahuzi-Biega National Park</a> (1980),\n<a href="/wiki/Salonga_National_Park" title="Salonga National Park">Salonga National Park</a> (1984) and\n<a href="/wiki/Okapi_Wildlife_Reserve" title="Okapi Wildlife Reserve">Okapi Wildlife Reserve</a> (1996).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Provinces">Provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Districts of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Districts of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Territories of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Territories of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Administrative divisions of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Administrative divisions of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>The country is currently divided into the city-province of Kinshasa and 25 other <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Provinces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">provinces</a>. The provinces are subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Districts of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">districts</a> which are divided into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Territories of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">territories</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup> Before 2015, the country had 11 provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table style="border-spacing: 20px 1px;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td rowspan="13"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a
