Province</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Wildlife of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Wildlife of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bas-congo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bas-congo.JPG/220px-Bas-congo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bas-congo.JPG/330px-Bas-congo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bas-congo.JPG/440px-Bas-congo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bas-congo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bas-Congo" title="Bas-Congo">Bas-Congo</a> landscape</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Okapi2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1482" data-file-width="1707" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Okapi2.jpg/220px-Okapi2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Okapi2.jpg/330px-Okapi2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Okapi2.jpg/440px-Okapi2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Okapi2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Okapi</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2488" data-file-width="2228" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg/220px-Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg/330px-Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg/440px-Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Male_gorilla_in_SF_zoo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A male <a href="/wiki/Western_gorilla" title="Western gorilla">Western gorilla</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hippo_pod_edit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2160" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Hippo_pod_edit.jpg/220px-Hippo_pod_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Hippo_pod_edit.jpg/330px-Hippo_pod_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Hippo_pod_edit.jpg/440px-Hippo_pod_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hippo_pod_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hippopotami" title="Hippopotami">Hippopotami</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforests</a> of the Democratic Republic of the Congo contain great <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, including many rare and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endemic_(ecology)" title="Endemic (ecology)">endemic</a> species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">common chimpanzee</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">bonobo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_forest_elephant" title="African forest elephant">African forest elephant</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">mountain gorilla</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Okapi" title="Okapi">okapi</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_rhino" title="White rhino">white rhino</a>. Five of the country\'s <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a> are listed as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Garamba_National_Park" title="Garamba National Park">Garumba</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kahuzi-Biega_National_Park" title="Kahuzi-Biega National Park">Kahuzi-Biega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salonga_National_Park" title="Salonga National Park">Salonga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga National Parks</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Okapi_Wildlife_Reserve" title="Okapi Wildlife Reserve">Okapi Wildlife Reserve</a>.\nThe Democratic Republic of the Congo is the most biodiverse African country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The civil war and resulting poor economic conditions have endangered much of this biodiversity. Many park wardens were either killed or could not afford to continue their work. All five sites are listed by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as World Heritage in Danger.\n</p><p>Conservationists have particularly worried about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primates" title="Primates">primates</a>. The Congo is inhabited by several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_ape" title="Great ape">great ape</a> species: the <a href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">common chimpanzee</a> (<i>Pan troglodytes</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">bonobo</a> (<i>Pan paniscus</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_gorilla" title="Eastern gorilla">eastern gorilla</a> (<i>Gorilla beringei</i>), and possibly the <a href="/wiki/Western_gorilla" title="Western gorilla">western gorilla</a> (<i>Gorilla gorilla</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> It is the only country in the world in which bonobos are found in the wild. Much concern has been raised about great ape extinction. Because of hunting and habitat destruction, the chimpanzee, the bonobo and the gorilla, each of whose populations once numbered in the millions, have now dwindled down to only about 200,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gorillas_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-gorillas-92">[92]</a></sup> gorillas, 100,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chimpanzees_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-chimpanzees-93">[93]</a></sup> chimpanzees and possibly only about 10,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chimpanzees_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-chimpanzees-93">[93]</a></sup> bonobos. Gorillas, chimpanzees, and bonobos are all classified as <a href="/wiki/Conservation_status" title="Conservation status">endangered</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Conservation_Union" title="World Conservation Union">World Conservation Union</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Okapi" title="Okapi">okapi</a>, which is also native to the area.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poaching">Poaching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Poaching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Poaching for the exotic animal or ivory trade has been a persistent problem for species loss in the DRC, it has been made a necessity for some trying to escape poverty and a means of continuing the civil war for some rebel groups including the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Resistance_Army" title="Lord\'s Resistance Army">Lords Resistance army</a> (LRA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The Forest Elephant is particularly at risk due to the high cost of its ivory, especially in the Far East, due to this its population has reduced by 62% in 2002&#8211;2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-95">[95]</a></sup> The main way this poaching for ivory can be reduced is through the hampering of the international demand for ivory, as this drives the trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The introduction of park guards and the implementation of eco-tourism in <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga National park</a>, a primary habitat for great apes, has allowed the endangered mountain gorilla population to jump over 1000, a 25% rise on 2010 numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-96">[96]</a></sup> However, the study indicated that poaching is still an existing problem, with researchers finding 380 snares and park guards continually being ambushed and killed by poachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Politics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Politics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_kabila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1973" data-file-width="1615" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joseph_kabila.jpg/170px-Joseph_kabila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joseph_kabila.jpg/255px-Joseph_kabila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joseph_kabila.jpg/340px-Joseph_kabila.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_kabila.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> has been President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo from January 2001 to January 2019.</div></div></div>\n<p>After a four-year interlude between two constitutions, with new political institutions established at the various levels of government, as well as new administrative divisions for the provinces throughout the country, a new constitution came into effect in 2006 and politics in the Democratic Republic of the Congo finally settled into a stable <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_republic" title="Democratic republic">democratic republic</a>.\nThe 2003 transitional constitution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> had established a parliament with a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> legislature, consisting of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Senate of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Senate</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="National Assembly of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">National Assembly</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Senate_(Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo)" title="Senate (Democratic Republic of the Congo)">Senate</a> had, among other things, the charge of drafting the new constitution of the country. The executive branch was vested in a 60-member cabinet, headed by a <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="President of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">President</a> and four vice presidents. The President was also the Commander-in Chief of the armed forces. The transitional constitution also established a relatively independent judiciary, headed by a Supreme Court with constitutional interpretation powers. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2006 constitution, also known as the Constitution of the Third Republic, came into effect in February 2006. It had concurrent authority, however, with the transitional constitution until the inauguration of the elected officials who emerged from the July 2006 elections. Under the new constitution, the legislature remained bicameral; the executive was concomitantly undertaken by a President and the government, led by a Prime Minister, appointed from the party able to secure a majority in the National Assembly.\n</p><p>The government&#160;&#8211; not the President&#160;&#8211; is responsible to the Parliament. The new constitution also granted new powers to the provincial governments, creating provincial parliaments which have oversight of the Governor and the head of the provincial government, whom they elect. The new constitution also saw the disappearance of the Supreme Court, which was divided into three new institutions. The constitutional interpretation prerogative of the Supreme Court is now held by the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Constitutional Court of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Constitutional Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although located in the Central African <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme" title="United Nations geoscheme">UN subregion</a>, the nation is also economically and regionally affiliated with Southern Africa as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Corruption in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Corruption in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>Mobutu Sese Seko ruled the DRC, which he renamed <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>, from 1965 to 1997. A relative explained how the government illicitly collected revenue: "Mobutu would ask one of us to go to the bank and take out a million. We\'d go to an intermediary and tell him to get five million. He would go to the bank with Mobutu\'s authority, and take out ten. Mobutu got one, and we took the other nine."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-a-101">[101]</a></sup> Mobutu institutionalized corruption to prevent political rivals from challenging his control, leading to an <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo#1990s" title="Economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">economic collapse in 1996</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-b-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mobutu allegedly stole as much as US$4&#8211;5 billion while in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-c-103">[103]</a></sup> He was not the first corrupt Congolese leader by any means: "Government as a system of organized theft goes back to King Leopold II," noted <a href="/wiki/Adam_Hochschild" title="Adam Hochschild">Adam Hochschild</a> in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AH_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-AH-104">[104]</a></sup> In July 2009, a Swiss court determined that the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_limitations" title="Statute of limitations">statute of limitations</a> had run out on an <a href="/wiki/International_asset_recovery" title="International asset recovery">international asset recovery</a> case of about $6.7 million of deposits of Mobutu\'s in a Swiss bank, and therefore the <a href="/wiki/Asset" title="Asset">assets</a> should be returned to Mobutu\'s family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> established the Commission of Repression of Economic Crimes upon his ascension to power in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-d-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1352" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg/220px-DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg/330px-DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg/440px-DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DRC-_Child_Soldiers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A group of demobilized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_soldiers" title="Child soldiers">child soldiers</a> in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Human rights in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Human rights in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_soldiers_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Child soldiers in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Child soldiers in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court_investigation_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> was initiated by Joseph Kabila in April 2004. The international Criminal Court prosecutor opened the case in June 2004.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_soldiers" title="Child soldiers">Child soldiers</a> have been used on a large scale in DRC, and in 2011 it was estimated that 30,000 children were still operating with armed groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrumbl201232_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrumbl201232-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Instances of child labor and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_labor" title="Forced labor">forced labor</a> have been observed and reported in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Labor" title="U.S. Department of Labor">U.S. Department of Labor</a>\'s <i>Findings on the Worst Forms of Child Labor</i> in the DRC in 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> and six goods produced by the country\'s mining industry appear on the department\'s December 2014 <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence_against_women">Violence against women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Violence against women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Sexual violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_macho-violence_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Military macho-violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Military macho-violence in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court_investigation_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">International Criminal Court investigation in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">Violence against women</a> seems to be perceived by large sectors of society to be normal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The 2013&#8211;2014 <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">DHS survey</a> (pp.&#160;299) found that 74.8% of women agreed that a husband is justified in beating his wife in certain circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_United_Nations" title="The United Nations">The United Nations</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Committee_on_the_Elimination_of_Discrimination_against_Women" title="Committee on the Elimination of Discrimination against Women">Committee on the Elimination of Discrimination against Women</a> in 2006 expressed concern that in the post-war transition period, the promotion of women\'s human rights and gender equality is not seen as a priority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Mass rapes, sexual violence and sexual slavery are used as a weapon of war by the Armed Forces of the Democratic Republic of the Congo and armed groups in the eastern part of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The eastern part of the country in particular has been described as the "rape capital of the world" and the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a> there described as the worst in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">Female genital mutilation</a> (FGM) is also practiced in DRC, although not on a large scale. The prevalence of FGM is estimated at about 5% of women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> FGM is illegal: the law imposes a penalty of two to five years of prison and a fine of 200,000 Congolese francs on any person who violates the "physical or functional integrity" of the genital organs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2007, the International Committee of the Red Cross expressed concern about the situation in eastern DRC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> A phenomenon of "pendulum displacement" has developed, where people hasten at night to safety. According to Yakin Ert&#252;rk, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Rapporteur" title="United Nations Special Rapporteur">UN Special Rapporteur</a> on Violence against Women who toured eastern Congo in July 2007, violence against women in North and South Kivu included "unimaginable brutality". Ert&#252;rk added that "Armed groups attack local communities, loot, rape, kidnap women and children, and make them work as sexual slaves".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In December 2008, GuardianFilms of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> released a film documenting the testimony of over 400 women and girls who had been abused by marauding militia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2010, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> reported a dramatic increase in the number of rapes in the Democratic Republic of the Congo, and researchers from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvard" title="Harvard">Harvard</a> discovered that rapes committed by civilians had increased seventeenfold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> In June 2014, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_from_Torture" title="Freedom from Torture">Freedom from Torture</a> published reported rape and sexual violence being used routinely by state officials in Congolese prisons as punishment for politically active women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomfromtorture.org_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-freedomfromtorture.org-124">[124]</a></sup> The women included in the report were abused in several locations across the country including the capital Kinshasa and other areas away from the conflict zones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomfromtorture.org_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-freedomfromtorture.org-124">[124]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, figures both inside and outside of the country, such as Filimbi and <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Weyi" title="Emmanuel Weyi">Emmanuel Weyi</a>, spoke out about the need to curb violence and instability as the 2016 elections approached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Foreign relations and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Foreign relations of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Foreign relations of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Military of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Military of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2640" data-file-width="3960" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/220px-Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/330px-Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/440px-Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Kabila_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in August 2014</div></div></div>\n<p>The global growth in demand for scarce raw materials and the industrial surges in China, India, Russia, Brazil and other <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> require that <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed countries</a> employ new, integrated and responsive strategies for identifying and ensuring, on a continual basis, an adequate supply of strategic and critical materials required for their security needs. Highlighting the DR Congo\'s importance to United States national security, the effort to establish an elite Congolese unit is the latest push by the U.S. to professionalize armed forces in this strategically important region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are economic and strategic incentives to bring more security to the Congo, which is rich in natural resources such as <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, a strategic and critical metal used in many industrial and military applications. The largest use of cobalt is in <a href="/wiki/Superalloy" title="Superalloy">superalloys</a>, used to make <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">jet engine</a> parts. Cobalt is also used in <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_alloy" title="Magnetic alloy">magnetic alloys</a> and in cutting and wear-resistant materials such as cemented <a href="/wiki/Carbide" title="Carbide">carbides</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical industry</a> consumes significant quantities of cobalt in a variety of applications including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalyst" title="Catalyst">catalysts</a> for petroleum and chemical processing; drying agents for paints and inks; ground coats for porcelain enamels; decolorant for ceramics and glass; and pigments for ceramics, paints, and plastics. The country possesses 80% of the world\'s cobalt reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="730" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg/220px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg/330px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg/440px-Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_GDP_evolution-fr.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Evolution of GDP</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Congo" title="Central Bank of the Congo">Central Bank of the Congo</a> is responsible for developing and maintaining the <a href="/wiki/Congolese_franc" title="Congolese franc">Congolese franc</a>, which serves as the primary form of <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> in the Democratic Republic of the Congo. In 2007, The World Bank decided to grant the Democratic Republic of Congo up to $1.3 billion in assistance funds over the following three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Kinshasa is currently negotiating membership in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohada.com_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-130">[130]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Democratic Republic of Congo is widely considered one of the world\'s richest countries in natural resources; its untapped deposits of raw minerals are estimated to be worth in excess of US$24 trillion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The Congo has 70% of the world\'s <a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">coltan</a>, a third of its <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, more than 30% of its diamond reserves, and a tenth of its copper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite such vast mineral wealth, the economy of the Democratic Republic of the Congo has declined drastically since the mid-1980s. The African country generated up to 70% of its export revenue from minerals in the 1970s and 1980s, and was particularly hit when resource prices deteriorated at that time. By 2005, 90% of the DRC\'s revenues derived from its minerals (Exenberger and Hartmann 2007:10).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ExenbergerHartmann2007_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-ExenbergerHartmann2007-136">[136]</a></sup> The country\'s woes mean that despite its potential its citizens are among the poorest people on Earth. DR Congo consistently has the lowest, or nearly the lowest, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">nominal GDP per capita</a> in the world. The DRC is also one of the twenty lowest-ranked countries on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corruption_Perception_Index" title="Corruption Perception Index">Corruption Perception Index</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Mining industry of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Mining industry of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diamonds-_Zaire,_(DR_Congo)_(8458935824).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="899" data-file-width="966" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg/220px-Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg/330px-Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg/440px-Diamonds-_Zaire%2C_%28DR_Congo%29_%288458935824%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diamonds-_Zaire,_(DR_Congo)_(8458935824).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rough diamonds ~1 to 1.5 mm in size from DR Congo.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC) is the world\'s largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a> ore,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and a major producer of <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>. The latter come from Kasai province in the west. By far the largest mines in the DRC are located in southern <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga province</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Shaba</a>), and are highly mechanized, with a capacity of several million tons per year of copper and cobalt ore, and refining capability for metal ore. The DRC is the second-largest diamond-producing nation in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> and artisanal and small-scale miners account for most of its production.\n</p><p>At independence in 1960, DRC was the second-most industrialized country in Africa after South Africa; it boasted a thriving mining sector and a relatively productive agriculture sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo Wars</a> began in 1996. These conflicts have dramatically reduced national output and government revenue, increased external debt, and resulted in deaths of more than five million people from war and associated <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> and disease. <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">Malnutrition</a> affects approximately two thirds of the country\'s population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Foreign businesses have curtailed operations due to uncertainty about the outcome of the conflict, lack of infrastructure, and the difficult operating environment. The war intensified the impact of such basic problems as an uncertain legal framework, corruption, inflation, and lack of openness in government economic policy and financial operations.\n</p><p>Conditions improved in late 2002, when a large portion of the invading foreign troops withdrew. A number of <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> missions met with the government to help it develop a coherent economic plan, and President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kabila" title="Joseph Kabila">Joseph Kabila</a> began implementing reforms. Much economic activity still lies outside the GDP data. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Development_Index" title="United Nations Human Development Index">United Nations Human Development Index</a> report shows that the human development index of DRC is one of the worst the country has had in decades. Through 2011 the DRC had the lowest Human Development Index of the 187 ranked countries. It ranked lower than <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, despite a higher margin of improvement than the latter country over 2010\'s numbers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_Congo,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="256" data-file-width="441" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/330px-Democratic_Republic_of_Congo%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Democratic_Republic_of_Congo,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>DR Congo\'s <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> scores, 1970&#8211;2010.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1754" data-file-width="2063" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg/220px-Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg/330px-Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg/440px-Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Basankusu_collecting_firewood_by_Francis_Hannaway.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Collecting firewood in <a href="/wiki/Basankusu" title="Basankusu">Basankusu</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The economy of DRC relies heavily on mining. However, the smaller-scale economic activity from <a href="/wiki/Artisanal_mining" title="Artisanal mining">artisanal mining</a> occurs in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Informal_sector" title="Informal sector">informal sector</a> and is not reflected in GDP data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> A third of the DRC\'s diamonds are believed to be smuggled out of the country, making it difficult to quantify diamond <a href="/wiki/Production_(economics)" title="Production (economics)">production</a> levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kitco_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kitco-141">[141]</a></sup> In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a> was discovered in the east of the country, but to date has only been mined on a small scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Smuggling of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_minerals" title="Conflict minerals">conflict minerals</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">coltan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cassiterite" title="Cassiterite">cassiterite</a>, ores of <a href="/wiki/Tantalum" title="Tantalum">tantalum</a> and tin, respectively, helped to fuel the war<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> in the Eastern Congo.\n</p><p>In September 2004, state-owned <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9camines" title="G&#233;camines">G&#233;camines</a> signed an agreement with Global Enterprises Corporate (GEC), a company formed by the merger of <a href="/wiki/Dan_Gertler" title="Dan Gertler">Dan Gertler International</a> (DGI) with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beny_Steinmetz_Global" title="Beny Steinmetz Global">Beny Steinmetz Global</a>, to rehabilitate and operate the <a href="/wiki/Kananga_Mine" title="Kananga Mine">Kananga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tilwezembe" title="Tilwezembe">Tilwezembe</a> copper mines. The deal was ratified by presidential decree. In 2007, a World Bank report reviewed DR Congo\'s three biggest mining contracts, finding that the 2005 deals, including one with Global Enterprises Company, were approved with "a complete lack of transparency" (Mahtani, 3 January 2007).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FinancialTimes20070103_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FinancialTimes20070103-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sergeant20070403_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sergeant20070403-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatangaHist_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-KatangaHist-146">[146]</a></sup> Gertler and Steinmetz put GEC\'s 75% share in Komoto Oliveira Virgule (KOV), the project made of up of Tilwezembe and Kananga, along with the Kolwesi concentrator, into <a href="/wiki/Nikanor_plc" title="Nikanor plc">Nikanor plc</a>. Registered in the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, reached a market capitalization of $1.5 billion by 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sergeant20070403_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sergeant20070403-145">[145]</a></sup> In February 2007, 22% of the Nikanor Mining company was owned by the Gertner Family Trust and 14% by <a href="/wiki/Dan_Gertler" title="Dan Gertler">Dan Gertler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> In January 2008 <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Mining" title="Katanga Mining">Katanga Mining</a> acquired Nikanor for $452 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatangaHist_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-KatangaHist-146">[146]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2006, Gertler\'s DGI took a major stake in DEM Mining, a cobalt-copper mining and services company based in Katanga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sergeant20070403_145-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sergeant20070403-145">[145]</a></sup> In June 2006, Gertler bought <a href="/wiki/Tremalt" title="Tremalt">Tremalt</a> from the Zimbabwean businessman <a href="/wiki/John_Bredenkamp" title="John Bredenkamp">John Bredenkamp</a> for about $60 million. Tremalt had a half share in the <a href="/wiki/Mukondo_Mine" title="Mukondo Mine">Mukondo Mine</a>. In 2007, Tremalt was owned by Prairie International Ltd, of which Dan Gertler\'s family trust was a major shareholder. Tremalt owned 80% of Savannah Mining, which held concessions C17 and C18 in Katanga Province and 50% of the Mukondo project. The other 50% of Mukondo was held by Boss Mining, which in turn was 80% owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_African_Mining_%26_Exploration_Company" title="Central African Mining &amp; Exploration Company">Central African Mining &amp; Exploration Company</a> (CAMEC). Boss Mining had rented and operated Bredenkamp\'s half of Mukondo. Gertler terminated this arrangement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sergeant20070403_145-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sergeant20070403-145">[145]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Katanga_Mining" title="Katanga Mining">Katanga Mining Limited</a>, a Swiss-owned company, owns the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luilu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luilu (page does not exist)">Luilu</a> Metallurgical Plant, which has a capacity of 175,000 tonnes of copper and 8,000 tonnes of cobalt per year, making it the largest cobalt refinery in the world. After a major rehabilitation program, the company resumed copper production operations in December 2007 and cobalt production in May 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2013, anti-corruption NGOs revealed that Congolese tax authorities had failed to account for $88 million from the mining sector, despite booming production and positive industrial performance. The missing funds date from 2010 and tax bodies should have paid them into the central bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Later in 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Extractive_Industries_Transparency_Initiative" title="Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative">Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative</a> suspended the country\'s candidacy for membership due to insufficient reporting, monitoring and independent audits, but in July 2013 the country improved its accounting and transparency practices to the point where the EITI gave the country full membership.\n</p><p>In February 2018, global asset management firm <a href="/wiki/AllianceBernstein" title="AllianceBernstein">AllianceBernstein</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> defined the DRC as economically "the Saudi Arabia of the electric vehicle age," due to its cobalt resources, as essential to the <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">lithium-ion batteries</a> that drive <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_train_in_Kindu,_DRC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg/220px-First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg/330px-First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg/440px-First_train_in_Kindu%2C_DRC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_train_in_Kindu,_DRC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Train from <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a> arriving in <a href="/wiki/Kindu" title="Kindu">Kindu</a> on a newly refurbished line.</div></div></div>\n<p>Ground transport in the Democratic Republic of Congo has always been difficult. The terrain and climate of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Basin" title="Congo Basin">Congo Basin</a> present serious barriers to road and rail construction, and the distances are enormous across this vast country. The DRC has more navigable rivers and moves more passengers and goods by boat and ferry than any other country in Africa, but air transport remains the only effective means of moving goods and people between many places within the country, especially in rural areas. Chronic economic mismanagement, political corruption and internal conflicts have led to long-term under-investment of infastructure.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Rail transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Rail transport in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Train_rdc.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="671" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/280px-Train_rdc.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/420px-Train_rdc.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Train_rdc.svg/560px-Train_rdc.svg.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Train_rdc.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of rail network</div></div></div>\n<p>Rail transportation is provided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_Railroad_Company" title="Congo Railroad Company">Congo Railroad Company</a> (Soci&#233;t&#233; Nationale des Chemins de Fer du Congo) and the <a href="/wiki/Office_National_des_Transports_(Congo)" title="Office National des Transports (Congo)">Office National des Transports (Congo)</a> (ONATRA) and the Office of the Uele Railways (Office des Chemins de fer des Ueles, CFU). Like much of the infrastructure in the Congo, the railways are poorly maintained, dirty, crowded and dangerous.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Democratic Republic of the Congo has fewer all-weather paved highways than any country of its population and size in Africa&#160;&#8212; a total of 2,250&#160;km (1,400&#160;mi), of which only 1,226&#160;km (762&#160;mi) is in good condition (see below). To put this in perspective, the road distance across the country in any direction is more than 2,500&#160;km (1,600&#160;mi) (e.g. Matadi to Lubumbashi, 2,700&#160;km (1,700&#160;mi) by road). The figure of 2,250&#160;km (1,400&#160;mi) converts to 35&#160;km (22&#160;mi) of paved road per 1,000,000 of population. Comparative figures for Zambia and Botswana are 721&#160;km (448&#160;mi) and 3,427&#160;km (2,129&#160;mi) respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Three routes in the <a href="/wiki/Trans-African_Highway_network" title="Trans-African Highway network">Trans-African Highway network</a> pass through DR Congo:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tripoli-Cape_Town_Highway" title="Tripoli-Cape Town Highway">Tripoli-Cape Town Highway</a>: this route crosses the western extremity of the country on National Road No. 1 between Kinshasa and <a href="/wiki/Matadi" title="Matadi">Matadi</a>, a distance of 285&#160;km (177&#160;mi) on one of the only paved sections in fair condition.</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lagos-Mombasa_Highway" title="Lagos-Mombasa Highway">Lagos-Mombasa Highway</a>: the DR Congo is the main missing link in this east-west highway and requires a new road to be constructed before it can function.</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beira-Lobito_Highway" title="Beira-Lobito Highway">Beira-Lobito Highway</a>: this east-west highway crosses <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga</a> and requires re-construction over most of its length, being an earth track between the Angolan border and <a href="/wiki/Kolwezi" title="Kolwezi">Kolwezi</a>, a paved road in very poor condition between Kolwezi and <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi" title="Lubumbashi">Lubumbashi</a>, and a paved road in fair condition over the short distance to the Zambian border.</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Democratic Republic of Congo has thousands of kilometres of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navigable" title="Navigable">navigable</a> <a href="/wiki/Waterway" title="Waterway">waterways</a>. Traditionally water transport has been the dominant means of moving around in approximately two-thirds of the country.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As of  June&#160;2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, DR Congo had one major national airline (<a href="/wiki/Congo_Airways" title="Congo Airways">Congo Airways</a>) that offered flights inside DR Congo. Congo Airways was based at <a href="/wiki/N%27djili_Airport" title="N\'djili Airport">Kinshasa\'s international airport</a>. All air carriers certified by the DRC have been banned from European Union airports by the European Commission, due to inadequate safety standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several international airlines service <a href="/wiki/N%27djili_Airport" title="N\'djili Airport">Kinshasa\'s international airport</a> and a few also offer international flights to <a href="/wiki/Lubumbashi_International_Airport" title="Lubumbashi International Airport">Lubumbashi International Airport</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>In the Democratic Republic of the Congo, there are both coal and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> resources that were mainly used domestically in 2008. The Democratic Republic of Congo has infrastructure for hydro-electricity from the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Inga_dams" title="Inga dams">Inga dams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The Democratic Republic of Congo also possesses 50% of Africa\'s forests and a river system that could provide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydro-electric" title="Hydro-electric">hydro-electric</a> power to the entire continent, according to a UN report on the country\'s strategic significance and its potential role as an economic power in central Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The generation and distribution of electricity is controlled by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_nationale_d%27%C3%A9lectricit%C3%A9_(SNEL)" title="Soci&#233;t&#233; nationale d\'&#233;lectricit&#233; (SNEL)">Soci&#233;t&#233; nationale d\'&#233;lectricit&#233; (SNEL)</a>, but only 15% of the country has access to electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>   The DRC a member of three electrical power pools. These are SAPP (Southern African Power Pool), EAPP (East African Power Pool), CAPP (Central African Power Pool.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy">Renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Renewable energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Renewable energy in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>Because of abundant sunlight, potential for solar development is very high in the DRC. There are already about 836 solar power systems in the DRC, with a total power of 83&#160;kW, located in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_%C3%89quateur" title="Province of &#201;quateur">&#201;quateur</a> (167), Katanga (159), Nord-Kivu (170), the two Kasa&#239; provinces (170), and Bas-Congo (170). Also, the 148 Caritas network system has a total power of 6.31&#160;kW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DRC_classroom.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1197" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/220px-DRC_classroom.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/330px-DRC_classroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/DRC_classroom.jpg/440px-DRC_classroom.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DRC_classroom.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A classroom in the Democratic Republic of the Congo.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate for the population between the ages of 15 and 49 was estimated to be 75.9% (88.1% male and 63.8% female) according to a <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">DHS</a> nationwide survey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The education system in the Democratic Republic of the Congo is governed by three government ministries: the <i>Minist&#232;re de l\'Enseignement Primaire, Secondaire et Professionnel (MEPSP</i>), the <i>Minist&#232;re de l\'Enseignement Sup&#233;rieur et Universitaire (MESU)</i> and the <i>Minist&#232;re des Affaires Sociales (MAS)</i>. Primary education in the Democratic Republic of the Congo is not free or compulsory,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> even though the Congolese constitution says it should be (Article 43 of the 2005 Congolese Constitution).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the 6-year civil war in the late 1990s-early 2000s, over 5.2 million children in the country did not receive any education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-160">[160]</a></sup> Since the end of the civil war, the situation has improved tremendously, with the number of children enrolled in primary schools rising from 5.5 million in 2002 to 13.5 million in 2014, and the number of children enrolled in secondary schools rising from 2.8 million in 2007 to 4.4 million in 2014 according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Actual school attendance has also improved greatly in recent years, with primary school net attendance estimated to be 82.4% in 2014 (82.4% of children ages 6&#8211;11 attended school; 83.4% for boys, 80.6% for girls).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Health in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Health in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="HIV/AIDS in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">HIV/AIDS in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="List of hospitals in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">hospitals in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa_General_Hospital" title="Kinshasa General Hospital">General Hospital of Kinshasa</a>. DRC has the world\'s second-highest rate of <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>). In April 2011, through aid from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GAVI_Alliance" title="GAVI Alliance">Global Alliance for Vaccines</a>, a new vaccine to prevent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pneumococcal_disease" title="Pneumococcal disease">pneumococcal disease</a> was introduced around <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, it was estimated that about 1.1% of adults aged 15&#8211;49 were living with <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> is also a problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">Yellow fever</a> also affects DRC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">Maternal health</a> is poor in DRC. According to 2010 estimates, DRC has the 17th highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, 43.5% of children under five are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stunted" title="Stunted">stunted</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_and_law_enforcement">Crime and law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Crime and law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Law enforcement in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Law enforcement in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>The Congolese National Police (PNC) are the primary police force in the Democratic Republic of the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Demographics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Demographics of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Poverty in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<h3><span
