style="text-align:right;">453,147\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kongo_people2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongo_people2.jpg/220px-Kongo_people2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongo_people2.jpg/330px-Kongo_people2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kongo_people2.jpg/440px-Kongo_people2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kongo_people2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a> youth and adults in <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa, Democratic Republic of Congo</a></div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">12.2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">47.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">78.7\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_the_Day,_17_February_2014_(12589890963).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1853" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg/220px-Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg/330px-Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg/440px-Photo_of_the_Day%2C_17_February_2014_%2812589890963%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_the_Day,_17_February_2014_(12589890963).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amani festival in <a href="/wiki/Goma" title="Goma">Goma</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg/220px-Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg/330px-Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg/440px-Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cecilia_and_her_family.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Family in Rutshuru, North Kivu, Democratic Republic of the Congo</div></div></div>\n<p>Over 200 ethnic groups populate the Democratic Republic of the Congo, of which the majority are <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a>. Together, <a href="/wiki/Mongo_people" title="Mongo people">Mongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luba_people" title="Luba people">Luba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a> peoples (Bantu) and <a href="/wiki/Mangbetu_people" title="Mangbetu people">Mangbetu</a>-<a href="/wiki/Zande_people" title="Zande people">Azande</a> peoples constitute around 45% of the population. The <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo people</a> are the largest ethnic group in the Democratic Republic of Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gates2010p14_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gates2010p14-175">[175]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, the United Nations estimated the country\'s population to be 79 million people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup> a rapid increase from 39.1 million in 1992 despite the ongoing war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> As many as 250 ethnic groups have been identified and named. The most numerous people are the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luba_people" title="Luba people">Luba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mongo_people" title="Mongo people">Mongo</a>. About 600,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_Pygmies" title="Congo Pygmies">Pygmies</a> are the aboriginal people of the DR Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Although several hundred local languages and dialects are spoken, the linguistic variety is bridged both by widespread use of French and the national intermediary languages <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kituba" title="Kituba">Kituba</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tshiluba_language" title="Tshiluba language">Tshiluba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingala_language" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(7134901927).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/220px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/330px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg/440px-Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_%287134901927%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opening_ceremony_of_new_PNC_headquarters_in_Goma_(7134901927).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population fleeing their villages due to fighting between FARDC and rebels groups, Sake North Kivu 30 April 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>Given the situation in the country and the condition of state structures, it is extremely difficult to obtain reliable migration data. However, evidence suggests that DRC continues to be a destination country for immigrants, in spite of recent declines in their numbers. Immigration is very diverse in nature; refugees and asylum-seekers&#160;&#8211; products of the numerous and violent conflicts in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">Great Lakes Region</a>&#160;&#8211; constitute an important subset of the population. Additionally, the country\'s large mine operations attract migrant workers from Africa and beyond. There is also considerable migration for commercial activities from other African countries and the rest of the world, but these movements are not well studied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-178">[178]</a></sup> Transit migration towards South Africa and Europe also plays a role.\n</p><p>Immigration to the DRC has decreased steadily over the past two decades, most likely as a result of the armed violence that the country has experienced. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, the number of immigrants in the DRC has fallen from just over 1 million in 1960, to 754,000 in 1990, to 480,000 in 2005, to an estimated 445,000 in 2010. Official figures are unavailable, partly due to the predominance of the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a> in the DRC. Data are also lacking on irregular immigrants, however given neighbouring countries\' ethnic links to DRC nationals, irregular migration is assumed to be a significant phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-178">[178]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Figures for Congolese nationals abroad vary greatly depending on the source, from 3 to 6 million. This discrepancy is due to a lack of official, reliable data. Emigrants from the DRC are above all long-term emigrants, the majority of whom live in Africa and to a lesser extent in Europe; 79.7% and 15.3% respectively, according to estimated 2000 data. New destination countries include South Africa and various points en route to Europe. The DRC has produced a considerable number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees">refugees</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asylum-seekers" title="Asylum-seekers">asylum-seekers</a> located in the region and beyond. These numbers peaked in 2004 when, according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>, there were more than 460,000 refugees from the DRC; in 2008, Congolese refugees numbered 367,995 in total, 68% of whom were living in other African countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOMProfile_178-2"><a href="#cite_note-IOMProfile-178">[178]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2003, more than 400,000 Congolese migrants have been expelled from <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>Christianity is the majority religion in the Democratic Republic of the Congo. The most recent survey, conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> Program in 2013-2014 indicated that Christians constituted 93.7% of the population (with Catholics making up 29.7%, Protestants 26.8%, and other Christians 37.2%). An indigenous religion, <a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a>, has the adherence of only 2.8%, while Muslims make up 1.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_2013-14_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2013-14-180">[180]</a></sup> Other recent estimates have found Christianity the majority religion, followed by 95.8% of the population according to a 2010 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-religion-181">[181]</a></sup> estimate, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> reports this figure to be 80%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> 2013 data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-religion2-182">[182]</a></sup> The proportion of followers of Islam is variously estimated from 1%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> to 10%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> depending on the source, and followers of indigenous beliefs similarly estimated to range from about 3&#8211;10% .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2_182-1"><a href="#cite_note-religion2-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_2013-14_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2013-14-180">[180]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are about 35 million Catholics in the country<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup> with six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese" title="Archdiocese">archdioceses</a> and 41 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dioceses" title="Dioceses">dioceses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> The impact of the Catholic Church in the Democratic Republic of Congo is difficult to overestimate. Schatzberg has called it the country\'s "only truly national institution apart from the state."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Its schools have educated over 60% of the nation\'s primary school students and more than 40% of its secondary students. The church owns and manages an extensive network of hospitals, schools, and clinics, as well as many diocesan economic enterprises, including farms, ranches, stores, and artisans\' shops.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a> was seen as a threat to the colonial regime and was banned by the Belgians. Kimbanguism, officially "the church of Christ on Earth by the prophet Simon Kimbangu", now has about three million members,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adherents_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adherents-187">[187]</a></sup> primarily among the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Bakongo</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bas-Congo" title="Bas-Congo">Bas-Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2178" data-file-width="4096" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/220px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/330px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png/440px-Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_notre_dame_de_la_victoire_bukavu.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Peace_Cathedral,_Bukavu" title="Our Lady of Peace Cathedral, Bukavu">Our Lady of Peace Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bukavu" title="Bukavu">Bukavu</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Sixty-two Protestant denominations are federated under the umbrella of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ_in_Congo" title="Church of Christ in Congo">Church of Christ in Congo</a>. It is often simply referred to as <i>the Protestant Church</i>, since it covers most of the DRC Protestants. With more than 25 million members, it constitutes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_Protestant_churches" title="List of the largest Protestant churches">one of the largest Protestant bodies</a> in the world.\n</p><p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pew_Forum" title="Pew Forum">Pew Forum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Islam in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Islam</a> is the faith of 12% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion2_182-2"><a href="#cite_note-religion2-182">[182]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>, Muslims make up 10% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-8"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup> Islam was introduced and mainly spread by traders/merchants/slave raiders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Congolose Muslims are divided into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunnis" title="Sunnis">Sunnis</a> (50%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia">Shias</a> (10%), <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadis</a> (6%), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a> (14%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> In 2013 the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Democratic_Forces" title="Allied Democratic Forces">Allied Democratic Forces</a>, a group linked to <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a>, began <a href="/wiki/Allied_Democratic_Forces#2013_resurgence" title="Allied Democratic Forces">carrying out attacks in Congo</a> which killed civilians, mostly Christians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first members of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i_Faith" title="Baha\'i Faith">Baha\'i Faith</a> to live in the country came from Uganda in 1953. Four years later the first local administrative council was elected. In 1970 the National Spiritual Assembly (national administrative council) was first elected. Though the religion was banned in the 1970s and 1980s, due to misrepresentations of foreign governments, the ban was lifted by the end of the 1980s. In 2012 plans were announced to build a national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i_House_of_Worship" title="Baha\'i House of Worship">Baha\'i House of Worship</a> in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Traditional religions embody such concepts as <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitalism" title="Vitalism">vitalism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spirit_worship" title="Spirit worship">spirit</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancestor_worship" title="Ancestor worship">ancestor worship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>, and sorcery and vary widely among ethnic groups. The syncretic sects often merge elements of Christianity with traditional beliefs and rituals and are not recognized by mainstream churches as part of Christianity. New variants of ancient beliefs have become widespread, led by US-inspired Pentecostal churches which have been in the forefront of witchcraft accusations, particularly against children and the elderly.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What is the new belief? Witchcraft, or the accusations of witchcraft? (January 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Children accused of witchcraft are sent away from homes and family, often to live on the street, which can lead to physical violence against these children.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What leads to violence? (January 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> The usual term for these children is <i>enfants sorciers</i> (child witches) or <i>enfants dits sorciers</i> (children accused of witchcraft). Non-denominational church organizations have been formed to capitalize on this belief by charging exorbitant fees for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exorcisms" title="Exorcisms">exorcisms</a>. Though recently outlawed, children have been subjected in these exorcisms to often-violent abuse at the hands of self-proclaimed prophets and priests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Source\n</th>\n<th width="90pt">Christianity<br/><small>(total)</small>\n</th>\n<th width="90pt">Catholicism\n</th>\n<th width="90pt">Protestantism\n</th>\n<th width="90pt">Islam\n</th>\n<th width="90pt">Other\n</th>\n<th width="90pt">Source\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_State_Department" title="US State Department">US State Department</a></i></td>\n<td>90%</td>\n<td>50%</td>\n<td>35%</td>\n<td>5%</td>\n<td>5%</td>\n<td><a class="external autonumber" href="https://www.state.gov/j/drl/rls/irf/religiousfreedom/index.htm#wrapper" rel="nofollow">[1]</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"><i><a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a></i></td>\n<td>96%</td>\n<td>47%</td>\n<td>48%</td>\n<td>1.5%</td>\n<td>2.5%</td>\n<td><a class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130101080244/http://features.pewforum.org/grl/population-percentage.php" rel="nofollow">[2]</a> <a class="external autonumber" href="http://features.pewforum.org/global-christianity/map.php#/africa,ALL" rel="nofollow">[3]</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left"><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a></i></td>\n<td>80%</td>\n<td>50%</td>\n<td>20%</td>\n<td>10%</td>\n<td>10%</td>\n<td><a class="external autonumber" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/geos/cg.html" rel="nofollow">[4]</a>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_-_DR_Congo,_major_languages.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="679" data-file-width="729" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/220px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/330px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg/440px-Map_-_DR_Congo%2C_major_languages.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_-_DR_Congo,_major_languages.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Major Bantu languages in the Congo</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Languages of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Languages of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>French is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. It is culturally accepted as the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> facilitating communication among the many different ethnic groups of the Congo. According to a 2014 <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">OIF</a> report, 33 million Congolese people (47% of the population) could read and write in French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> In the capital city <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a>, 67% of the population could read and write French, and 68.5% could speak and understand it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Approximately 242 languages are spoken in the country, but only four have the status of national languages: <a href="/wiki/Kituba_language" title="Kituba language">Kituba</a> ("Kikongo ya leta"), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingala_language" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tshiluba_language" title="Tshiluba language">Tshiluba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>. Although some people speak these regional, or trade languages as first languages, most of the population speak them as a second language after their own tribal language. Lingala was the official language of the colonial army, the "<a href="/wiki/Force_Publique" title="Force Publique">Force Publique</a>", under Belgian colonial rule, and remains to this day the predominant language in the armed forces. Since the recent rebellions, a good part of the army in the East also uses Swahili where it is prevalent.\n</p><p>When the country was a Belgian colony, the Belgian colonizers instituted teaching and use of the four national languages in primary schools, making it one of the few African nations to have had literacy in local languages during the European colonial period. This trend was reversed after independence, when French became the sole language of education at all levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lang_educ_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-lang_educ-197">[197]</a></sup> Since 1975, the four national languages have been reintroduced in the first two years of primary education, with French becoming the sole language of education from the 3rd year onwards, but in practice many primary schools in urban areas solely use French from the first year of school onward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lang_educ_197-1"><a href="#cite_note-lang_educ-197">[197]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hemba_male_figure1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="853" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/170px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/255px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hemba_male_figure1.jpg/340px-Hemba_male_figure1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hemba_male_figure1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemba" title="Hemba">Hemba</a> male statue</div></div></div>\n<p>The culture of the Democratic Republic of the Congo reflects the diversity of its hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> and their differing ways of life throughout the country&#160;&#160;&#8212; from the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">River Congo</a> on the coast, upriver through the <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> in its centre, to the more densely populated mountains in the far east. Since the late 19th century, traditional ways of life have undergone changes brought about by <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, the struggle for independence, the stagnation of the Mobutu era, and most recently, the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo Wars</a>. Despite these pressures, the <a href="/wiki/Convention_(norm)" title="Convention (norm)">customs</a> and cultures of the Congo have retained much of their individuality. The country\'s 81 million inhabitants (at close of 2016) are mainly rural. The 30% who live in urban areas have been the most open to <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western</a> influences.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Another feature in Congo culture is its music. The DRC has blended its ethnic musical sources with Cuban <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_Rumba" title="Cuban Rumba">rumba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Merengue_music" title="Merengue music">merengue</a> to give birth to <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">soukous</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Other African nations produce music genres derived from Congolese soukous. Some of the African bands sing in <a href="/wiki/Lingala" title="Lingala">Lingala</a>, one of the main languages in the DRC. The same Congolese soukous, under the guidance of "le sapeur", <a href="/wiki/Papa_Wemba" title="Papa Wemba">Papa Wemba</a>, have set the tone for a generation of young men always dressed up in expensive designer clothes. They came to be known as the fourth generation of Congolese music and mostly come from the former well-known band <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wenge_Musica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wenge Musica (page does not exist)">Wenge Musica</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wenge_Musica" title="fr:Wenge Musica">fr</a>]</span>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Many sports are played in the Democratic Republic of the Congo, including <a href="/wiki/Football_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Football in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">football</a>, basketball, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Rugby union in the Democratic Republic of the Congo">rugby</a>. The sports are played in numerous stadiums throughout the country, including the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Frederic_Kibassa_Maliba" title="Stade Frederic Kibassa Maliba">Stade Frederic Kibassa Maliba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup>\nAs Zaire they have participated in the World Cup Football (Final stage) in 1974.\n</p><p>Internationally, the country is especially famous for its professional basketball <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA" title="NBA">NBA</a> and football players. <a href="/wiki/Dikembe_Mutombo" title="Dikembe Mutombo">Dikembe Mutombo</a> is one of the best African basketball players to ever play the game. Mutombo is well known for humanitarian projects in his home country. <a href="/wiki/Bismack_Biyombo" title="Bismack Biyombo">Bismack Biyombo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Eyenga" title="Christian Eyenga">Christian Eyenga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Mudiay" title="Emmanuel Mudiay">Emmanuel Mudiay</a> are others who gained significant international attention in basketball. Several Congolese players and players of Congolese descent&#8212;including strikers <a href="/wiki/Romelu_Lukaku" title="Romelu Lukaku">Romelu Lukaku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yannick_Bolasie" title="Yannick Bolasie">Yannick Bolasie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dieumerci_Mbokani" title="Dieumerci Mbokani">Dieumerci Mbokani</a>&#8212;have gained prominence in world football. DR Congo has twice won the African Cup of Nations football tournament.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congolese_cuisine" title="Congolese cuisine">Congolese cuisine</a></div>\n<p>Congolese cuisine is based on maiz, a mixture of maiz with boiling water and sometimes flour.  This mixture is called "fufu" in Lingala, "bukali" in Swahili, and "tshibele" in Tshiluba.  It\'s an important meal in DRC, the most important meal.  Everybody can eat it with fish, chicken, or as a meal.  It depends on your choice.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Media of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Media of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a></div>\n<p>Newspapers of the DRC include <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Avenir_(newspaper)" title="L\'Avenir (newspaper)">L\'Avenir</a></i>, <i>Radion T&#233;l&#233;vision Mwangaza</i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Conscience&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Conscience (page does not exist)">La Conscience</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Conscience" title="fr:La Conscience">fr</a>]</span></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=L%27Observateur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="L\'Observateur (page does not exist)">L\'Observateur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%27Observateur_(RDC)" title="fr:L\'Observateur (RDC)">fr</a>]</span></i>, <i>Le Phare</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Potentiel" title="Le Potentiel">Le Potentiel</a></i>, <i>Le Soft</i> and <i>LeCongolais.CD</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> a web-based daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Radio T&#233;l&#233;vision Nationale Congolaise (RTNC) is the national broadcaster of the Democratic Republic of the Congo. RTNC currently broadcasts in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingala_language" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>, French, and English.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_writers" title="List of Democratic Republic of the Congo writers">Congolese authors</a> use literature as a way to develop a sense of <a href="/wiki/National_consciousness" title="National consciousness">national consciousness</a> amongst the Congo people. The tragic history of colonialism and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">war</a> lead the Congolese people to settle in a place of complacency, accepting the culture that was forced upon them by <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgium</a>.\n</p><p>The Belgian attitude was paternalism, training and treating Africans as if they were children. Belgian parliament replaced the privately owned free state. This acceptance led to a diffusion of language, and many Congolese people spoke, and wrote in <a href="/wiki/French_Congo" title="French Congo">French</a>.\n</p><p>Modern Congolese literature began to emerge in the late 1950s. There are a few rare pieces of literature dated back to before <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_I)" title="East African Campaign (World War I)">WWI</a>, but it was not until about 1954 that literature written in French made its appearance in the Congo. After gaining their independence from Belgium in the 1960s, new authors, such as Guy Menga and Jean Pierre Makouta-Mboukou, were inspired by older authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Jean_Malonga" title="Jean Malonga">Jean Malonga</a>, and used writing to bring attention to new issues affecting the Congo. The rise of female authors began in the 1970s introducing diversity to Congolese literature and support for gender empowerment. Many authors who have contributed to the success of Congolese literature are now living abroad due to economic and political issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Kambemba_Yamusangie" title="Frederick Kambemba Yamusangie">Frederick Kambemba Yamusangie</a> writes literature for the between generations of those who grew up in the Congo, during the time when they were colonised, fighting for independence and after. Yamusangie in an interview<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> said he felt the distance in literature and wanted to remedy that he wrote the novel, Full Circle, which is a story of a boy named Emanuel who in the beginning of the book feels a difference in culture among the different groups in the Congo and elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%AFs_Neza_Boneza" title="Ra&#239;s Neza Boneza">Rais Neza Boneza</a>, an author from the <a href="/wiki/Katanga_Province" title="Katanga Province">Katanga province</a> of the Democratic Republic of Congo, wrote novels and poems to promote artistic expressions as a way to address and deal with conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Born in 1907, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Malonga" title="Jean Malonga">Jean Molonga</a>, was a novelist and storyteller, who sat in parliament from 1946 to 1951. He was noted for his original work, <i>Coeur d\'Aryenne</i>, Heart of Aryenne, consisting of controversial themes; cultural identity, national unity, and reformation of the oppressed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup>\n</p><p>These authors, along with others, used their platforms to bring awareness to the crises and conflicts that took place in the Congo.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A dense <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a> in the DRC\'s central <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">river basin</a> and eastern highlands is bordered on the east by the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift" title="Albertine Rift">Albertine Rift</a> (the western branch of Africa\'s <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley" title="Great Rift Valley">Great Rift System</a>). It includes several of Africa\'s Great Lakes.\n</p><p><b>Major environmental issues</b>\n</p><p>DR Congo\'s major environmental issues include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a></li>\n<li>poaching, which threatens wildlife populations</li>\n<li>water pollution</li>\n<li>mining</li></ul>\n<p>Displaced refugees cause or are otherwise responsible for significant deforestation, soil erosion and wildlife poaching. Another significant issue is environmental damage from mining of minerals, especially diamonds, gold, and <a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">coltan</a> &#8211; a mineral used to manufacture <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capacitors" title="Capacitors">capacitors</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Species_and_Biodiversity_loss">Species and Biodiversity loss</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Species and Biodiversity loss">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mountain_gorilla_(Gorilla_beringei_beringei)_yawn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="3132" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg/220px-Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg/330px-Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg/440px-Mountain_gorilla_%28Gorilla_beringei_beringei%29_yawn.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mountain_gorilla_(Gorilla_beringei_beringei)_yawn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The endangered Mountain Gorilla, half of its population live in the DRC\'s <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga National Park</a>, making the park critical habitat for these animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The environmental problems associated with The Democratic Republic of Congo (DRC) affect it\'s many endemic species of flora and fauna. The DRC has the worlds second largest contiguous rain forest after the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon</a> as well as other ecosystems including Savanna, swamps and flood plains. According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>, these unique habitats and species make the DRC one of the most valuable yet vulnerable areas in the world for biodiversity, wildlife protection and rainforest sustainability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Species loss has been cited as a problem in the DRC, brought about or exacerbated by reasons that include deforestation for mining, wood fuel, infrastructure or agriculture, war, illegal poaching and increased consumption of bush meat due to overpopulation and lack of food security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Some attempts to combat species loss in countries such as the DRC are actions such as the UN\'s Sustainable Development Goals (SDG), specifically SDG 15 Life on Land, the primary goals of which is to increase reforestation and biodiversity and reduce species loss, desertification, and illegal poaching.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> One of the primary defences for species and habitat protection in the DRC is its system of national parks and reserves, which gives protected status to nearly 12% of the DRC\'s rainforest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-211">[211]</a></sup> Five of these parks and reserves are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_world_heritage" title="UNESCO world heritage">UNESCO world heritage</a> sites, including Africa&#8217;s first national park <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga national park</a>.  All of these parks have been put on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_in_Danger" title="List of World Heritage in Danger">World Heritage in Danger List</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Poor governance and low economic conditions have reduced the effectiveness of these protections, especially during war times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-211">[211]</a></sup> The human cost of protecting these parks has also been high with 200 park ranger deaths in the past 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virunga_National_Park" title="Virunga National Park">Virunga national park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salonga_National_Park" title="Salonga National Park">Salongo National Park</a>, both of which are <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> world heritage sites are currently being looked at for mining and oil exploration. The move would open 21.5% of the Virunga park for exploitation, this is highly criticised by animal rights activists as it would threaten the habitat of <a href="/wiki/Mountain_gorilla" title="Mountain gorilla">Mountain Gorillas</a> and other endangered species.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Deforestation">Deforestation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Deforestation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Between 2000 and 2014 the DRC lost an average of 570,000 hectares (0.2%) of rainforest to deforestation per year, with the highest amount of deforestation coming between 2011 and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Deforestation is the primary cause of biodiversity reduction and species loss globally, through habitat loss and fragmentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> One of the goals of the SDG 15 is to reduce deforestation and encourage reforestation by 2020\n</p><p>The DRC has Africa&#8217;s largest rainforest, which is under the threat of deforestation through mining operations, agriculture, infrastructure and wood fuel. In the DRC 94% of wood taken from the rainforest is used for wood fuel, mainly due to poverty, lack of energy infrastructure and the decentralised nature of its population. To mitigate this aid agencies have tried to promote agro-forestry with fast growing trees to avoid over exploitation of the rainforests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Other large drivers of deforestation include mining and conflict, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Congo conflict</a> deforestation by militia groups was high for wood fuel, small mining operations and illegal logging to fund their operations. However, conversely conflict reduced deforestation for large scale mining due to security instability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_211-2"><a href="#cite_note-:4-211">[211]</a></sup>\n</p><p>One policy being attempted to reduce the deforestation and increase biodiversity in the DRC is the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_REDD_Programme" title="United Nations REDD Programme">UN-REDD</a> program, which uses emissions trading system so that developed nations can off set their carbon emissions by paying developing nations with rainforest to manage and conserve their forest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bush_meat">Bush meat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Bush meat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Bush meat refers to any meat which is procured from the wild, as overpopulation and continual conflicts in the DRC has led to food shortages this has therefore increased the use of bush meat. Although, data on bush meat use is not extensive, studies estimate 6 million tonnes of animals are taken for bush meat globally each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-218">[218]</a></sup> What animals are hunted are done so indiscriminately without thought of the importance of certain species that could be <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_engineer" title="Ecosystem engineer">eco-system engineers</a> or <a href="/wiki/Keystone_species" title="Keystone species">keystone species</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_218-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-218">[218]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bush meat is an important source of protein for millions in the DRC, especially in rural areas where it makes up 50-70% of meals and for some who cannot afford farmed produce it is a free meal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> A recent study in the DRC revealed that almost all of the animals are taken from the Congo each year, at 93% of all live animals there are in the forest are extracted for bush meat, whereas a sustainable rate would be 20%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-220">[220]</a></sup> This is a huge amount compared to the Amazon where bush meat is hunted at only 3% the rate of the Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-220">[220]</a></sup> the study reveals the only way to solve this is to find other food sources to feed people in the Congo Basin as bush meat is their only means of eating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_220-2"><a href="#cite_note-:6-220">[220]</a></sup> Another study showed that the species of bush meat in the meat markets of the DRC\'s third largest city <a href="/wiki/Kisangani" title="Kisangani">Kisangani</a> were primarily <a href="/wiki/Even-toed_ungulate" title="Even-toed ungulate">Artiodactyla</a> at 40.06% of the carcasses sold then <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primates</a> at 37.79% of carcasses sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Recently the prevalence of hunting for bush meat has declined because of the risk to hunters and butchers from the <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_disease" title="Ebola virus disease">Ebola virus</a> from specifically ape and bat meat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-:7-222">[222]</a></sup> Even though when the meat is cooked smoked or dried it kills the virus, business has dropped significantly with some hunters reporting as much of a reduction in sales of 80%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-:7-222">[222]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflicts">Conflicts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Conflicts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>There has been a war in the DRC in different levels of intensity since 1994 when the country was called <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-223">[223]</a></sup> Although what was known as <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Africas World War</a> had ended in 2003 the Eastern part of the country still has on-going skirmishes between rebel groups and government forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-223">[223]</a></sup> No other method has reduced species population so dramatically than conflict, when a militia reached the <a href="/wiki/Garamba_National_Park" title="Garamba National Park">Garamba National Park</a> in 1997 with in 3 months, half of the parks elephants two thirds of the buffalos and three quarters of its hippos vanished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-224">[224]</a></sup> The reason conflict is so damaging to wildlife is the increased use of bushmeat to feed soldiers, the prevalence of weapons, the lucrative industry of selling exotic animals and ivory as well as the general failure of law and order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_224-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-224">[224]</a></sup> According to another study, which was taken during the time of the civil war in the <a href="/wiki/Okapi_Wildlife_Reserve" title="Okapi Wildlife Reserve">Okapi Faunal Reserve</a> there was a 50% reduction in the abundance of elephants and a vast change in the distribution of them to the more secluded areas of the park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: See fonctionnelle des organes g&#233;nitaux d&#8217;une personne. Lorsque la mutilation a entra&#238;n&#233; la mort, la peine est de servitude p&#233;nale &#224; perp&#233;tuit&#233;."</i><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140819085226/http://monusco.unmissions.org/LinkClick.aspx?fileticket=aXFfmf5vsm8%3D&amp;tabid=11245&amp;mid=14386&amp;language=en-US" rel="nofollow">"Archived copy"</a>.
